Three Exceptions to the One-Third Rule in Wills
Explains three exceptions to the one-third rule with examples and calculations

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the three Hanafi exceptions where a will exceeding one third is valid without heirs' consent and explain the reasoning behind each exception.

Core Idea
A will exceeding one third is valid without heirs’ consent in muhabah, sa'ayah, and darahim mursalah.

By default, a will for more than one third of the estate requires the consent of the heirs. But the Hanafi school recognizes three exceptional cases where the will is effective up to one third even without permission. These exceptions are based on the nature of the bequest – whether it is a favoritism in sale, a partial emancipation with work, or a fixed sum that may not exceed the estate. Understanding these exceptions is crucial for applying the law of wills correctly.

Guided Path
1
Identify the general rule and its exception
The general rule is that a will for more than one third is invalid unless the heirs consent. The passage states that the Imam (Abu Hanifa) made exceptions for three specific situations: muhabah (favoritism in sale), sa'ayah (working off freedom for slaves), and darahim mursalah (unspecified dirhams).
These exceptions apply even when the bequest exceeds one third.
2
Analyze the reasoning behind the exceptions
When a will specifies a fraction like half or two-thirds, the excess is explicit and the will is considered void for the excess – the legatee only gets one third. But when a will is for a fixed sum (like fifty dirhams) that coincidentally exceeds one third of the current estate, the will is not void because the amount might turn out to be less than one third if the estate grows. The three exceptions follow a similar logic.
The key distinction: explicit fraction vs. fixed sum.
3
Examine the muhabah example
A man has two slaves worth 1100 and 600. He wills that each be sold to different persons for 100. The favoritism is 1000 and 500. If the estate is only these two slaves and heirs do not consent, the one third of the estate (1700/3 ≈ 566.66) is divided between the legatees in proportion to their favoritism (2:1).
Under the general rule, the legatee with the larger favoritism would get only one third of the estate (i.e., 566.66), but here he gets two-thirds of that one third.
4
Examine the sa'ayah example
A man wills to free two slaves worth 1000 and 2000, with no other assets. If heirs do not consent, both are freed from one third of the estate (1000). Each is freed from part of their value without payment: the slave worth 1000 gets freed from 333.33 dirhams (one third of his value) and must work for the remaining 666.66; the slave worth 2000 gets freed from 666.66 (one third of his value) and works for 1333.33.
Under the general rule, the division would be equal (half and half) because the legatees would be allocated only one third each, but here it is proportional to value.
5
Examine the darahim mursalah example
A man wills 1000 to one person and 2000 to another, with an estate of 3000 (one third = 1000). Heirs do not consent. The one third is divided in the ratio of the bequests (1:2), so the first receives 333.33 and the second 666.66. Under the general rule, they would share equally (500 each).
The exception applies because the bequests are specified as absolute sums, not as fractions.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الوصية بثلث المال ونحوه بأكثر من الثلث إلا في المحاباة والسعاية والدراهم المرسلة - فكذا هذا وله : أن الموصى له يضرب بما يستحقه، وهو لا يستحق ما وراء الثلث إلا بإجازة الورثة، ولم يوجد، إلا أن الإمام استثنى من هذا الحكم الصور الثلث المذكورة بقوله: "إلا في المحاباة" إلخ، ووجه الفرق له بين هذه الصور الثلاث وبين غيرها أن الوصية إذا كانت مقدرة بما زاد على الثلث صريحا كالنصف والثلثين، والشرع أبطل الوصية في الزائد يكون ذكره لغوا، فلا يعتبر في حق الضرب، بخلاف ما إذا لم تكن مقدرة حيث لا يكون في العبارة ما يكون مبطلا للوصية كما إذا أوصى بخمسين، واتفق أن ماله مائة فإن الوصية غير باطلة بالكلية لإمكان أن يظهر له فوق المائة، وإذا لم تبطل بالكلية تكون معتبرة في حق الضرب. (فتح) درهم ذلك من إلا في المحاباة: أي لا يضرب للموصى له بأكثر من الثلث إذا لم تجز الورثة إلا في هذه الصور الثلاث، وصورة المحاباة: أن يكون له عبدان قيمة أحدهما ألف ومائة، وقيمة الآخر ست مائة وأوصى بأن يباع واحد منهما بمائة لفلان، والآخر بمائة لفلان ،آخر ، فقد حصلت المحاباة لأحدهما بألف درهم، ولآخر بخمس مائة، فإن خرج ثلث ماله، أو أجازت الورثة جاز ذلك، وإن لم يكن له مال غيرهما، ولم تجز الورثة جاز محاباتهما بقدر الثلث، فيكون الثلث بينهما أثلاثا يضرب الموصى له بالألف بحسب وصيته، وهي الألف، والموصى له الآخر بحسب وصيته وهي خمس مائة، فلو كان هذا كسائر الوصايا وجب أن لا يضرب الموصى له بالألف بأكثر من خمس مائة وستة وستين وثلثي درهم عند الإمام؛ لأن عنده الموصى له بأكثر من الثلث لا يضرب إلا بالثلث، وهذا ثلث ماله. رمز الحقائق: ٤٧٧/٢] والسعاية صورة السعاية أن يوصى بعتق هذين العبدين قيمة أحدهما ألف وقيمة الآخر ألفان، ولا مال له غيرهما، فإن أجازت الورثة يعتقان معا، وإن لم تجز الورثة يعتقان من الثلث وثلث ماله ألف، فيكون الثلث منه للذي قيمته ألف فيعتق منه هذا القدر بجانا، وهو ثلاث مائة وثلاثة وثلاثون درهما وثلث درهم، ويسعى في الباقي، وهو الثلثان ستمائة وستة وستون درهما وثلثا ،درهم والثلثان منه للذي قيمته ألفان، فيعتق . منه هذا القدر بلا سعاية، وهو ست مائة وستة وستون وثلثا درهم، ويسعى في الباقي، وهو ألف وثلاث مائة وثلاثة وثلاثون وثلث درهم، فلو كان كسائر الوصايا وجب أن يسعى الذي قيمته ألف في خمس مائة نصف قيمته، والذي قيمته ألفان في ألف وخمس مائة ثلاثة أرباع قيمته؛ لأنه حينئذ لا يضرب الذي قيمته ألفان إلا بالألف، فوجب أن يكون بينهما نصفان رمز الحقائق: ٤٧٧/٢] والدراهم المرسلة إلخ [أي المطلقة عن كونها ثلثا أو نصفا أو نحوهما. (طائي)] صورة الدراهم المرسلة: أن لأحدهما بألف ولآخر بألفين وثلث ماله ألف، ولم تجز الورثة، يكون الثلث بينهما أثلاثا، يضرب كل واحد منهما بقدر له بالألف، ثلثه ثلاث مائة وثلاثة وثلاثون وثلث درهم وللموصى له بألفين، ضعفه ست مائة وستة حقه، فللموصى وستون وثلثا درهم، وكان قياس أصل أبي حنيفة أن يكون الألف بينهما نصفين رمز الحقائق: ٤٧٧/٢]
The will of one third of wealth and similar: with more than one third except in muhabah, sa'ayah, and unspecified dirhams. So this is the same. And for him: that the legatee is allocated according to what he deserves, and he does not deserve what is beyond one third except with the permission of the heirs, and it did not occur, except that the Imam excepted from this ruling the three mentioned forms by his saying: 'except in muhabah' etc. And the face of the difference for him between these three forms and others is that if the will is specified as exceeding one third explicitly, like half or two thirds, and the Law invalidates the will in the excess, its mention becomes meaningless, so it is not considered in the allocation. Unlike if it is not specified, where there is nothing in the expression that invalidates the will, as if he wills fifty dirhams and it happens that his wealth is one hundred, the will is not entirely invalid because it is possible that his wealth turns out to be more than one hundred, and if it is not entirely invalid, it is considered in the allocation. (Fath) ... except in muhabah: i.e., the legatee is not allocated more than one third if the heirs do not permit, except in these three forms. The form of muhabah: that he has two slaves, the value of one is one thousand and one hundred, and the value of the other is six hundred, and he wills that one of them be sold for one hundred to so-and-so, and the other for one hundred to another so-and-so. So favoritism occurred for one by one thousand dirhams, and for the other by five hundred. If one third of his wealth is available, or the heirs permit, it is valid. If he has no other wealth besides them, and the heirs do not permit, their favoritism is valid up to one third, so the one third is divided between them in thirds: the legatee of the one thousand is allocated according to his will, which is the one thousand, and the other legatee according to his will, which is five hundred. If this were like other wills, the legatee of the one thousand should not be allocated more than five hundred sixty-six and two-thirds dirhams according to Imam Abu Hanifa, because according to him, the legatee of more than one third is allocated only one third, and this is one third of his wealth. (Ramz al-Haqa'iq 2/477) And sa'ayah: the form of sa'ayah is that he wills the emancipation of these two slaves, the value of one is one thousand and the value of the other is two thousand, and he has no other wealth besides them. If the heirs permit, both are freed together. If the heirs do not permit, both are freed from one third, and one third of his wealth is one thousand. So from the one third, the one worth one thousand gets freed from this amount without payment: three hundred thirty-three and one-third dirhams, and he works for the rest, which is two-thirds: six hundred sixty-six and two-thirds dirhams. And two-thirds of it is for the one worth two thousand, he gets freed from this amount without payment: six hundred sixty-six and two-thirds dirhams, and he works for the rest: one thousand three hundred thirty-three and one-third dirhams. If this were like other wills, the one worth one thousand should work for five hundred (half of his value), and the one worth two thousand for one thousand five hundred (three-quarters of his value), because then the one worth two thousand is allocated only one thousand, so it should be half and half between them. (Ramz al-Haqa'iq 2/477) And the unspecified dirhams etc. [meaning free from being one third or half or the like. (Tai)] The form of unspecified dirhams: that one has one thousand and another has two thousand, and one third of his wealth is one thousand, and the heirs do not permit. The one third is divided between them in thirds: each is allocated according to his right. For the legatee of one thousand, his third is three hundred thirty-three and one-third dirhams, and for the legatee of two thousand, double that: six hundred sixty-six and two-thirds dirhams. And the analogy of Abu Hanifa's principle was that the one thousand should be half between them. (Ramz al-Haqa'iq 2/477)
Source pages p. 482

Commentary
This passage is an expansion on a ruling from the matn regarding wills that exceed one third of the estate. The author explains that while the default rule is that a will for more than one third is ineffective without the heirs' consent, there are three exceptions: muhabah (favoritism in sale), sa'ayah (working off freedom for slaves), and darahim mursalah (unspecified dirhams). The key reasoning is that when the will specifies an amount exceeding one third (like half), the excess is void and the legatee only gets one third. But when the will is for a specific amount that coincidentally exceeds one third (like fifty dirhams when the estate is one hundred), the will is still valid for one third because it wasn't intended to exceed. The Imam (Abu Hanifa) made an exception for these three cases even when the will is for a specific amount. The passage then gives detailed examples of each case with calculations, showing how the one third is divided among legatees proportionally to their bequests, and contrasts this with how it would be handled under the general rule.

Key Terms
المحاباة (al-muhabah): Favoritism in a sale, e.g., selling valuable items cheaply as part of a will.
السعاية (al-sa'ayah): The work a slave must do to earn freedom when partially freed by a will exceeding one third.
الدراهم المرسلة (al-darahim al-mursalah): Unspecified dirhams: a will for a sum of money not designated as a fraction of the estate.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) Equally, each gets half of one third
B) In proportion to their favoritism: one gets two-thirds of one third, the other gets one-third
C) The legatee of the more valuable slave gets the entire one third
D) The legatee of the less valuable slave gets the entire one third

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school carves out three exceptions where a will exceeding one third is valid without heirs' consent, based on the nature of the bequest as a fixed sum or specific act rather than an explicit fraction.

Distinguishing Valid and Invalid Bequests: 'Like the Share of My Son' vs 'The Share of My Son'
Distinguishes bequests of specific vs similar shares

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on bequeathing 'the share of my son' vs 'like the share of my son', explain the reason for the distinction, and apply it to similar cases.

Core Idea
A bequest of another's property is invalid; bequeathing 'the share of my son' is invalid because that share is not owned by the testator.

The precise wording of a will can determine its validity. In this passage, the Hanafi school distinguishes between two similar phrases: 'the share of my son' (nasib ibnihi) and 'like the share of my son' (mithl nasib ibnihi). The first is invalid if the testator has a son, while the second is valid. Understanding this distinction requires analyzing ownership at the time of the will. Let's walk through the reasoning.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two phrases and their rulings
The passage states: bequeathing 'the share of my son' is invalid (batil), while bequeathing 'like the share of my son' is valid (sahih). Note that this applies only if the testator has a son; if he has no son, the first is also valid.
The key is the testator's ownership at the time of the will.
2
Understand the legal reason (illa) for invalidity
The son's share (nasib al-ibn) is what the son will inherit after death. At the time of the will, that share does not belong to the testator; it is a future right of the son. Hence, bequeathing it is a bequest of another's property, which is invalid.
In contrast, 'like the share of my son' refers to an amount equivalent to the son's share, which is the testator's own property.
3
Consider the exception when the testator has no son
If the testator has no living son at the time of death, the phrase 'the share of my son' has no referent and is treated as a bequest of an unspecified portion. The text notes it becomes valid in that case.
This shows the ruling is conditional on the existence of a son.
4
Examine Zufar's objection and the Hanafi response
Zufar argued that bequeathing 'the share of my son' is always valid because all property is owned by the testator at present, and the mention of the son's share is merely for estimation. The Hanafi response is that the son's share is determined after death and is not the testator's property at the time of the will.
This is a legitimate ikhtilaf; the Hanafi view is the relied-upon position.
5
Apply the rule to calculate shares with multiple sons
If the testator has two sons and bequeaths 'like the share of my son', the legatee gets one third (as if he were an additional son), not half. The preferred view is that the testator intended the legatee to be treated as a son, not to exceed any son's share.
If the testator has one son, the legatee gets half, but if heirs do not consent, only one third.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
يوصي بنصيب ابنه بطل، وبمثل نصيب ابنه صح، فإن كان له ابنان، فله الثلث، وبسهم أو للموصي للموصى له أي لو أوصى بسهم جزء من ماله فالبيان إلى الورثة فإن قال : سدس مالي لفلان، ثم قال: له ثلث مالي، له ثلث ماله وإن قال: سدس مالي لفلان ثم قال له سدس مالي، له السدس. للموصى له وإن أوصى بثلث دراهمه أو غنمه، وهلك ثلثاه، له ما بقي، بطل: هذا إذا كان له ابن وإن لم يكن له ابن فالوصية جائزة، وقال زفر جاز مطلقا؛ لأن الكل ماله في الحال، وذكر نصيب الابن للتقدير، ولنا أن نصيب الابن ما يصيبه بعد الموت، فكان وصية مال الغير، بخلاف ما إذا أوصى بمثل نصيب ابنه؛ لأن مثل الشيء غيره. (عيني، فتح) صح ويكون ذلك وصية بنصف المال إذا كان له ابن واحد، فإن أجازه جاز، وإلا لكان له الثلث. (فتح) فإن كان إلخ : أي فإن كان للموصي ابنان، فللموصى له الثلث، والقياس أن يكون له النصف عند إجازة الورثة؛ لأنه أوصى له بمثل نصيب ابنه، ونصيب كل واحد منهما النصف وجه الأول: أنه قصد أن يجعل له مثل ابنه لا أن يزيد نصيبه على نصيب ابنه، وذلك بأن يجعل الموصى له كأحدهم. رمز الحقائق: ٤٧٨/٢] وفي كلام المصنف تفكيك الضمير، فلو أتى بالظاهر مكان الضمير في قوله: "فله الثلث" بأن قال: فللموصى له الثلث لكان أولى. (فتح)
He bequeaths the share of his son: invalid. And bequeathing like the share of his son: valid. If he has two sons, then he has one third. And [bequeathing] a share or a part of his wealth: the clarification is up to the heirs. If he says: one sixth of my wealth is for so-and-so, then he says: he has one third of my wealth, then he has one third of his wealth. And if he says: one sixth of my wealth is for so-and-so, then he says: he has one sixth of my wealth, then he has one sixth. And if he bequeaths one third of his dirhams or his sheep, and two-thirds perish, he has what remains. Invalid: this is if he has a son; if he does not have a son, the will is valid. Zufar said: it is valid absolutely, because all of it is his property at present, and the mention of the son's share is for estimation. For us (Hanafis): the son's share is what he gets after death, so it is a bequest of another's property, unlike if he bequeaths like the share of his son, because like of a thing is other than it. ('Ayni, Fath) Valid: and that is a will of half the property if he has one son; if he permits, it is valid, otherwise he has one third. (Fath) 'If he has' etc.: i.e., if the testator has two sons, then the legatee gets one third. The analogy is that he should get half if the heirs permit, because he bequeathed like the share of his son, and each son's share is half. The first view is preferred: that he intended to make him like a son, not to increase his share over the son's share, so the legatee is treated as one of them. (Ramz al-Haqa'iq 2/478) And in the author's words there is pronoun confusion; if he had used the explicit instead of the pronoun in his saying 'he has one third', he should have said 'the legatee has one third' which would be better. (Fath)
Source pages p. 483

Commentary
This passage addresses the validity of a will that uses the phrase 'the share of my son' versus 'like the share of my son'. The ruling is that bequeathing 'the share of my son' is invalid because the son's share is not yet determined at the time of the will and belongs to the son after the testator's death, so it is a bequest of another's property. However, bequeathing 'like the share of my son' is valid because it means an amount similar to what the son will receive, which is the testator's own property. If the testator has one son, this amounts to half the estate (since the son takes half as a residuary heir), but if the heirs do not permit, the legatee gets only one third. If the testator has two sons, the legatee gets one third (equal to one son's share), and the preferred view is that he is treated as an additional son, not exceeding any son's share. The passage also notes a grammatical issue: the author used a pronoun that could cause confusion.

Key Terms
نصيب الابن (nasib al-ibn): The specific share that the son inherits from the testator's estate, determined after death.
مثل نصيب الابن (mithl nasib al-ibn): An amount equal to the son's share, considered a separate property of the testator and therefore a valid bequest.

Key Terms from Source Passage

C) Because the son's share is not owned by the testator at the time of the will
D) Because the will is ambiguous and cannot be executed

Key Takeaway
Bequeathing a specific share of an heir is invalid because it is not owned; bequeathing an equivalent amount is valid.

Rulings on Ambiguous Bequests, Successive Bequests, and Lost Property
Rulings on ambiguous bequests, successive bequests, and lost property

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi rulings for ambiguous bequests (sahm/juz'), successive bequests, and bequest of a specific asset that partially perishes, and explain the internal Hanafi ikhtilaf on the interpretation of 'sahm'.

Core Idea
A will is not invalidated by ambiguity; heirs determine an ambiguous share, and if a specific bequest perishes, the legatee takes all that remains.

This lesson covers three distinct but interconnected rulings in Hanafi wasaya (law of wills). First, when a testator leaves an ambiguous portion like 'a share', the will remains valid and the heirs determine the amount. Second, if two bequests are made to the same person, the larger overrides the smaller. Third, if a specific asset bequeathed partially perishes, the legatee is entitled to all that remains of that asset. We will examine the internal differences of opinion within the Hanafi school and the opposing views of Zufar and Malik.

Guided Path
1
Distinguish between ambiguous and specific bequests
Identify whether the testator left an undefined share (e.g., 'a share' or 'a part') or a defined share of a specific asset. This determines which ruling applies.
The term 'sahm' (share) is ambiguous; the school differs on its meaning.
2
Apply the ruling for ambiguous bequests
If the bequest is vague, the heirs may determine the amount. Note the difference between Abu Hanifa (one sixth) and the two Companions (minimum heirs' share up to one third). The preferred view is that of the two Companions.
The text from al-Majma' is the relied-upon position.
3
Handle successive bequests
If the testator first wills one sixth then later wills one third to the same person, the later overrides and the legatee gets one third. If the same amount is repeated, only one sixth is due.
This is based on the principle that a definite noun repeated as definite refers to the same thing.
4
Analyze bequest of a specific asset that partially perishes
If the testator wills one third of a specific set of dirhams or sheep, and two-thirds perish before death, the legatee gets all that remains (the surviving one third). Contrast with Zufar and Malik who hold that loss is shared proportionally.
The Hanafi reasoning: the will attaches to that specific third, so it becomes the whole remaining.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فالبيان إلى الورثة فيقال لهم: أعطوه ما شئتم؛ لأنه مجهول يتناول القليل والكثير والوصية لا تمنع بالجهالة، والورثة قائمون مقام الموصي، فكان إليهم بيانه وسوّى الشيخ ههنا بين السهم والجزء، وهو اختيار بعض المشايخ والمروي عن أبي حنيفة: أن السهم عبارة عن السدس، نقل ذلك عن ابن مسعود له، وفي "المجمع": ولو أوصى : رصى بسهم من ماله فله أخس سهام الورثة عند أبي حنيفة، ولا يزاد على السدس؛ لأن مخرج السدس أعدل المخارج، فلا يتجاوز عنه كما في الإقرار وقالا له أخس سهام الوصايا، إلا أن يزيد على الثلث، فيكون له الثلث؛ لأن محل الوصية الثلث [رمز الحقائق: ٤٧٨/٢] فإن قال إلخ: أي إن قال رجل سدس مالي لفلان ،وصية، ثم قال في ذلك المجلس أو في مجلس آخر: له أي للذي أوصى له أولا بسدس ،ماله ثلث مالي فللموصى له ثلث ماله؛ لأن الثلث متضمن للسدس، فيدخل فيه، فلا يتناول أكثر من الثلث. (ملا مسكين، عيني بزيادة) له سدس مالي: أي يكون للموصى له سدس واحد، سواء قال ذلك في مجلس واحد أو في مجلسين؛ لأن المعرف إذا أعيد معرفا كان الثاني عين الأول. [رمز الحقائق: ٤٧٨/٢] وإن أوصى إلخ: أي إذا أوصى بثلث دراهمه أو ثلث غنمه، فهلك ثلثاه أي ثلثا الدراهم أو ثلثا الغنم، وبقي ثلثه، وهو يخرج من ماله فله جميع ما بقي من الدراهم أو الغنم، وقال زفر له ثلث ما بقي من ذلك النوع؛ لأن التركة مشتركة بين حقين فما هلك هلك عليهما، وبه قال مالك، ولنا أن الوصية تعلقت بثلث هذه، فإذا هلك الثلثان تعين الثلث لذلك. عيني بزيادة يسيرة من التكملة)
Then the clarification is up to the heirs; it is said to them: Give him whatever you wish, because it is unknown, covering little and much, and a will is not prevented by ignorance. The heirs stand in the place of the testator, so clarification is up to them. The Sheikh made no distinction here between share (sahm) and part (juz'), and this is the choice of some shaykhs. And it is narrated from Abu Hanifa that sahm (share) means one sixth, transmitted from Ibn Mas'ud. In al-Majma': If he wills a share of his wealth, he gets the least of the heirs' shares according to Abu Hanifa, and is not increased beyond one sixth, because the denominator of one sixth is the most just of denominators, so it is not exceeded as in iqrar. And the two Companions (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) said: he gets the least of the wills' shares, unless it exceeds one third, then he gets one third, because the place of will is one third. [Ramz al-Haqa'iq 2/478] Then if he says etc.: If a man says: one sixth of my wealth is for so-and-so as a will, then he says in the same sitting or another sitting: he (meaning the one he first willed one sixth) has one third of my wealth, then the legatee gets one third of his wealth, because the one third includes the one sixth, so it enters it, so it does not exceed one third. (Mulla Miskin, 'Ayni with addition) He has one sixth of my wealth: i.e., he gets only one sixth, whether he said it in one sitting or two, because a definite noun repeated as definite refers to the same thing. [Ramz al-Haqa'iq 2/478] And if he wills etc.: If he wills one third of his dirhams or one third of his sheep, then two-thirds of them perish, and one third remains, and that comes from his wealth, then he gets all that remains of the dirhams or sheep. Zufar said: he gets one third of what remains of that type, because the estate is shared between two rights, so what perishes is lost to both. Malik also said this. For us (Hanafis): the will is attached to one third of these (specific items), so when two-thirds perish, the one third is determined for that. ('Ayni with slight addition from al-Takmila)
Source pages p. 483

Commentary
This passage covers three sub-rulings. First: if the testator bequeaths a vague 'share' or 'part' of his wealth, the determination of the amount is left to the heirs, because the will is valid despite ambiguity, and the heirs stand in the testator's place. There is a difference of opinion: the preferred view (some shaykhs) equates 'share' with 'part', meaning any unspecified portion. But according to Abu Hanifa, 'share' means one sixth, based on a report from Ibn Mas'ud. However, the view in al-Majma' is that the legatee gets the smallest share of the heirs (to avoid exceeding one third) but not more than one sixth. The two Companions (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) say he gets the smallest of wills' shares, up to one third. Second: if the testator makes two bequests, first one sixth then later one third, the legatee gets one third because the later overrides and includes the earlier. If he says one sixth twice, he gets only one sixth. Third: if the testator bequeaths one third of a specific asset (like dirhams or sheep), and two-thirds of that asset are lost, the legatee is entitled to all that remains of that asset (i.e., the surviving one third), because the will is attached to that specific third. Zufar and Malik disagreed, saying the loss should be shared proportionally, but the Hanafi view is preferred.

Key Terms
السهم (al-sahm): An unspecified portion in a will; according to Abu Hanifa it means one sixth, but according to the two Companions it means the least of the heirs' shares up to one third.
الجزء (al-juz'): A part or fraction, treated similarly to 'sahm' in this context.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) One third of the remaining dirhams
B) All remaining dirhams
C) Nothing, because the subject matter perished
D) One ninth of the original dirhams

Key Takeaway
Hanafi law validates ambiguous bequests by leaving clarification to heirs, and in the case of a specific bequest that partially perishes, the legatee is entitled to all remaining property of that type.

Bequest of a Third of Non-Fungible Property When Part Perishes
Ruling on bequest of a third of non-fungible property when part perishes

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi ruling for a bequest of a third of slaves, clothes, or houses when part of that category perishes before death, and distinguish between fungible (same jins) and non-fungible (different jins) property.

Core Idea
If bequeathed property of different genres perishes, the legatee takes a third of what remains.

Imagine a testator bequeaths one-third of his slaves, but two-thirds of those slaves die before his death. Should the legatee receive one-third of the original number or one-third of the survivors? The Hanafi school answers with a nuanced rule based on the nature of the property. This passage explains how the legatee's share is calculated when the bequest is of a specific genre (slaves, clothes, houses) and part of that genre perishes, and it introduces the key concept of jins (genre) that determines whether the property is treated as fungible or not.

Guided Path
1
Identify the bequest type
Determine what was bequeathed: is it a third of a specific category (e.g., slaves, clothes, houses) or a third of the entire estate?
2
Assess what perished
Check if part of that specific category perished before the testator's death. The ruling applies when two-thirds of that category are lost.
3
Classify the property by jins
Determine whether the items within the category are of the same genre (jins wahid) or different genres (ajnas mukhtalifa). This affects how the remaining property is valued.
For example, clothes of different types (e.g., silk, cotton) are different jins; all dirhams are the same jins.
4
Apply the ruling for different jins
If the category consists of different genres (e.g., slaves of various nationalities, clothes of different fabrics), the legatee receives one-third of what remains of that category at death.
This is the ruling attributed to Zufar and the Hanafi school.
5
Distinguish the same-jins case
If the category is of one genre (e.g., all clothes of the same type), treat it like dirhams (fungible), and the ruling is different (likely the legatee gets one-third of the original).
The passage notes this exception but does not detail the ruling for fungibles.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الوصية بثلث المال ونحوه ولو رقيقا أو ثيابا أو دورا، له ثلث ما بقي أي إذا أوصى بثلث رقيقه أو ثيابه أو دوره، فهلك ثلثا ذلك، وبقي الثلث، فللموصى له ثلث ما بقي، كما قال زفر؛ لأن الجنس مختلف فلا يمكن جمعه بخلاف الأول على ما بينا قال هذا إذا كانت الثياب من أجناس مختلفة، وإن كانت من جنس واحد فهي بمنزلة الدراهم، وكذا كل مكيل وموزون كالدراهم لما بينا، وقيل: هذا قول أبي حنيفة في الرقيق والدور، وقيل: هو قول الكل.
The book of bequests. Bequest of a third of property and the like. And if he bequeaths a third of his slaves, or clothes, or houses, he gets a third of what remains. That is, if he bequeaths a third of his slaves, or clothes, or houses, and two-thirds of that perish, and one-third remains, then the legatee gets a third of what remains, as Zufar said, because the genre is different so it cannot be combined, unlike the first case as we explained. He said this if the clothes are of different genres; if they are of one genre, they are like dirhams, and likewise every measured or weighed item like dirhams as we explained. It is said: This is the saying of Abu Hanifa regarding slaves and houses, and it is said: It is the saying of all.
Source pages p. 484

Commentary
This passage states a ruling for bequest of a third of specific types of property (slaves, clothes, houses) when two-thirds of that type perish before death. The ruling is that the legatee receives one-third of the remaining third, following Imam Zufar's opinion. The reasoning is that these items are not fungible (different genres), so they cannot be combined with other property to satisfy the bequest. If the clothes are all of the same type, they are treated like dirhams (fungible). The ruling is attributed to Abu Hanifa or to all Hanafi scholars.

Key Terms
رقيق (raqeeq): Slaves, considered as a category of property
جنس (jins): Genre or type of property (e.g., slaves, clothes, houses)

Key Terms from Source Passage

B) One-third of the original clothes
C) One-third of the remaining clothes
D) All of the remaining clothes

Key Takeaway
When a bequest is of a third of a specific category of different-genre property, and two-thirds of that category perish, the legatee takes one-third of what remains.

Bequest of Fixed Amount with Cash and Debt
Ruling on bequest of fixed amount with mixed assets

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling for satisfying a bequest of a fixed amount when the testator has both cash and debts, and explain the talil (reasoning) that justifies proportional payment from debt collections.

Core Idea
A bequest is satisfied proportionally from cash and debts, treating the legatee as a partner with the heirs.

This lesson examines the Hanafi ruling on a bequest of a specific sum (e.g., 1000 dirhams) when the testator leaves both cash (ayn) and debts (dayn) owed to him. The ruling ensures fairness between the legatee and the heirs by paying the legatee from cash first, then from each debt collection as it materializes. The underlying reasoning (talil) explains the legal status of debt and the partnership-like relationship between the parties.

Guided Path
1
Identify the scenario and the bequest
The testator bequeaths a fixed amount (1000 dirhams) and leaves behind both cash (present property) and debts (receivables). Determine the total assets and the bequest amount.
The bequest is executed from one-third of the estate; here we assume the bequest is within the permissible one-third.
2
Apply the ruling for cash
If one-third of the cash suffices to cover the entire bequest, the legatee is paid fully from cash. Otherwise, he receives one-third of the cash as an initial payment.
The third of the cash is calculated from the total cash, not the estate.
3
Apply the ruling for debt collections
Whenever any debt is recovered after the testator's death, the legatee receives one-third of that collected amount. This continues until the full bequest is paid.
The legatee does not wait for all debts to be collected; he gets periodic payments.
4
Understand the reasoning (talil)
The text argues that the legatee is like a partner with the heirs: nothing is given to him until double goes to the heirs. Restricting him to cash alone would prejudice the heirs. Moreover, debt is not considered property until collected, as shown by the oath analogy.
This reasoning is based on fairness and the nature of debt in Hanafi fiqh.
5
Note the legal principle about debt
Debt (dayn) is not considered mal (property) for all purposes; it becomes property only upon recovery. Hence, the bequest attaches proportionally to each recovery.
This principle is demonstrated by the example of an oath: swearing 'I have no property' while having debts is not broken.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وبألف وله عين ودين، فإن خرج الألف للموصي نقد على الناس من ثلث العين دفع إليه وإلا فثلث العين، وكلما خرج شيء من الدين، له ثلثه حتى بعد ذلك يستوفي الألف أي إذا أوصى بألف درهم وله عين ودين، فإن خرج الألف من ثلث العين دفع إليه؛ لأن إيفاء حق كل واحد ممكن من غير بخس بأحد تكملة البحر الرائق: ٢٩٤/٩ وإلا فثلث العين إلخ: أي إن لم يخرج الألف من ثلث العين دفع إلى الموصى له ثلث العين، ثم كلما خرج شيء من الدين دفع إليه ثلثه حتى يستوفي حقه الألف؛ لأن الموصى له شريك الوارث في الحقيقة، ألا ترى أنه لا يسلم له شيء حتى يسلم للورثة ضعفه، وفي تخصيصه بالعين بخس بالورثة؛ لأن العين مقدمة على الدين ولأن الدين ليس بمال في مطلق الحال، ولهذا لو حلف أنه لا مال له، وله دين على الناس لا يحنث، وإنما يصير مالا عند الاستيفاء، وباعتباره تتناوله الوصية، فيعتدل النظر بقسمة كل واحد منهما من الدين والعين أثلاثا تكملة البحر الرائق: ٢٩٥/٩
And [if he bequeaths] one thousand dirhams, and he has cash and debt, if the thousand comes out of the third of the cash, it is given to him; otherwise, the third of the cash, and whenever something of the debt comes out, he gets its third until he recovers the thousand afterwards. That is, if he bequeaths a thousand dirhams and he has cash and debt, if the thousand comes out of the third of the cash, it is given to him because fulfilling each right is possible without injustice to anyone. Otherwise, the third of the cash is given to the legatee, then whenever something of the debt comes out, its third is given to him until he recovers his right of the thousand; because the legatee is in reality a partner with the heirs, do you not see that nothing is given to him until double is given to the heirs, and to restrict him to cash would be unjust to the heirs because cash is given priority over debt, and debt is not property in absolute terms, hence if someone swears that he has no property and he has a debt due from people, he does not break his oath, but it becomes property upon recovery. And in consideration of this, the bequest encompasses it, so the view is balanced by dividing each of them from debt and cash into thirds.
Source pages p. 484

Commentary
This passage deals with a bequest of a fixed amount (1000 dirhams) when the testator has both cash (ayn) and debts (dayn) owed to him. The ruling is that the legatee is first paid from the cash if the third of the cash suffices. If not, he is given one-third of the cash, and then whenever any debt is collected, he receives one-third of that collected amount until he gets the full 1000. The reason is that the legatee is like a partner with the heirs, and to give him only cash would prejudice the heirs. Also, debt is not considered property until collected, so the bequest attaches to it proportionally.

Key Terms
عين (ayn): Cash or tangible property in hand
دين (dayn): Debt owed to the testator, not yet collected
ثلث (thulth): One-third, the maximum share of the estate that can be bequeathed

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
If a testator has 100 dirhams cash and 900 dirhams in debts, and bequeaths 1000 dirhams, how is the legatee paid?
A) He receives 100 dirhams cash immediately
B) He receives 100 dirhams cash and then 30 from each debt collection
C) He receives nothing until all debts are collected
D) He receives 33.33 from the cash and 33.33 from each debt collection

Key Takeaway
When a testator leaves cash and debts, the legatee of a fixed sum is paid proportionally: one-third of cash first, then one-third of each debt collection, reflecting the partnership-like relationship with heirs and the nature of debt.

Bequest to Two Persons, One Deceased: The Hanafi-Imam Abu Yusuf Dispute
Ruling on bequest of one-third to two persons when one predeceases testator

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain why the Hanafi school holds that a bequest to a predeceased legatee is void and evaluate Imam Abu Yusuf’s distinction based on the testator’s knowledge.

Core Idea
A bequest to a dead person is void; the surviving legatee takes the entire third.

This passage deals with a common scenario in inheritance: a testator bequeaths one-third of his estate to two individuals, but one of them has already died before the testator. The Hanafi school, led by Abu Hanifa and Muhammad al-Shaybani, rules that the deceased legatee cannot receive anything, so the entire third goes to the surviving legatee. However, Imam Abu Yusuf introduces a nuance based on the testator's knowledge of the death. Understanding this dispute and the underlying principle of eligibility helps clarify when a bequest is valid and how shares are allocated.

Guided Path
1
State the main Hanafi position
Identify the ruling attributed to Abu Hanifa and Muhammad: if one legatee is dead at the time of bequest, the entire third goes to the surviving legatee.
The reasoning: a dead person is not eligible to receive a bequest (laysa bi-ahl li al-wasiyyah).
2
Identify Abu Yusuf’s variant
Note Abu Yusuf's view: if the testator did not know of the death, the bequest to the deceased is considered valid in his view, so the surviving legatee only gets half the third.
The distinction hinges on the testator's knowledge: if known, the bequest to the dead is void, and the living takes all.
3
Analyze the timing principle
Understand the principle: when a competing legatee 'exits' from the bequest – whether from the origin (already dead at time of bequest) or after the offer (dies later) – determines the share allocation.
If the legatee never entered (dead at offer), the surviving legatee gets all. If he entered then exited (died later), his share reverts to the testator's heirs, not to the co-legatee.
4
Apply the principle to two scenarios
Work through the examples: (a) Amr dead at time of bequest (origin) → Zayd gets all; (b) Amr alive at bequest then dies before testator → Zayd gets half, other half to testator's heirs.
This distinction is crucial for practical application.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وبثلثه لزيد وعمرو، وهو ميت لزيد كله؛ لأن الميت ليس بأهل للوصية، فلا يشارك الحي الذي هو أهل كما إذا أوصى لزيد وجدار، وعن أبي يوسف: أنه إذا لم يعلم بموته - له نصف الثلث؛ لأن الوصية عنده صحيحة لعمرو، فلم يوص للحي إلا بنصف الثلث، بخلاف ما إذا علم بموته؛ لأن الوصية لعمرو لم تصح فكان راضيا للحي بكل الثلث، هذا إذا خرج المزاحم من الأصل، أما إذا خرج بعد صحة الإيجاب يخرج بحصته كما إذا قال: ثلث مالي لفلان ولفلان ابن عبد الله إن مت، وهو فقير، فمات الموصي وفلان بن عبد كان لفلان نصف الثلث، ولذا قال الشارح ملا مسكين أما إذا كان عمرو حيا ثم مات، فلزيد نصف الثلث، والنصف الآخر لورثة الموصي إن مات عمرو قبل الموصي، وإن مات بعده، فنصيبه من لورثته، وأصله أنه متى دخل في الوصية ثم خرج لفقد شرطه، فلا يوجب الزيادة في حق الآخر، ومتى لم يدخل في الوصية لفقد الأهلية كان الكل للآخر.
And [if he bequeaths] his third to Zayd and Amr, and he (Amr) is dead, it is all for Zayd because the dead person is not qualified to receive a bequest, so he does not share with the living person who is qualified, just as if he bequeathed to Zayd and a wall. And from Abu Yusuf: if he did not know of his death, he gets half the third because in his view the bequest to Amr is valid, so he did not bequeath to the living except half the third, unlike if he knew of his death because the bequest to Amr is invalid, so he is content for the living with the whole third. This if the competing party exits from the origin; but if he exits after the validity of the offer, he exits with his share, as if he said: 'One-third of my property to so-and-so and to so-and-so son of Abdullah if I die, and he is poor,' then the testator dies and so-and-so son of Abdullah was [poor?], then so-and-so gets half the third. Hence the commentator Mulla Miskeen said: If Amr was alive then died, Zayd gets half the third, and the other half goes to the testator's heirs if Amr died before the testator, and if after, his share goes to his heirs. The principle is that when one enters the bequest then exits due to lack of condition, it does not cause an increase for the other, and when he never entered due to lack of qualification, the entire amount is for the other.
Source pages p. 484

Commentary
This passage addresses the case where a testator bequeaths one-third to Zayd and Amr, but Amr dies before the testator. The Hanafi ruling (attributed to Abu Hanifa and Muhammad) is that the entire third goes to Zayd, because a dead person cannot be a legatee. However, Abu Yusuf distinguishes: if the testator did not know of Amr's death at the time of the bequest, the bequest to Amr is considered valid (according to Abu Yusuf), so Zayd only gets half. But if the testator knew, the bequest to Amr is void, and Zayd gets the whole. The passage also discusses the scenario where the competing legatee was alive at the time of bequest but later died, applying the principle of when the exit occurs.

Key Terms
مزاحم (muzahim): A competing legatee who shares the bequest
وصية (wasiyyah): Bequest or will

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to Abu Hanifa, if a testator bequeaths one-third to Zayd and Amr, and Amr died before the testator (unknown to testator), what does Zayd receive?
A) One-third of the bequest
B) Half of the bequest
C) The entire bequest
D) Nothing

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi law, a bequest to a deceased person is void, and the entire share goes to the surviving co-legatee.

Bequest 'Between' Two Persons, One Dead
Ruling on bequest 'between' two when one is dead

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the ruling when a testator uses 'between' and one beneficiary predeceases, and distinguish it from the ruling when 'and' is used.

Core Idea
When a testator says 'between', the bequest is divided equally; if one dies, the survivor gets only his share, not the whole.

In the previous lesson, we saw that when a testator says 'one-third to Zayd and Amr' and one dies, the survivor takes the entire third. But what if the testator uses the word 'between'? The Hanafi school holds that 'between' inherently implies division. This lesson examines that distinction and its practical effect.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two expressions
Contrast the phrasing 'to Zayd and Amr' (previous lesson) with 'between Zayd and Amr' (current lesson). Note the key word is 'bayna' (between).
2
State the ruling for 'between'
When the testator says 'between Zayd and Amr' and Amr is dead, Zayd does NOT take the whole third; he takes half of it (one-sixth of the estate).
The other half goes to the testator's heirs.
3
Explain the linguistic reason
The word 'bayna' implies division and sharing. Its inherent meaning is that each named party is entitled to an equal portion.
This differs from the conjunction 'wa' (and) which does not necessarily imply division.
4
Apply to the hypothetical
If the testator says 'one-third between so-and-so' and is silent (i.e., names only one person), that person gets only half the third, not the whole.
This reinforces that 'between' always splits the amount equally.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ولو قال: ثلث مالي بين زيد وعمرو، وعمرو ميت كان لزيد نصف الثلث؛ لأن مقتضى هذا اللفظ أن يكون لكل واحد منهما الثلث، بخلاف ما تقدم، ألا ترى أن من قال: ثلث مالي لفلان وسكت، كان له كل الثلث ولو قال: ثلث مالي بين فلان وسكت لا يستحق الثلث كله بل نصفه.
And if he said: 'One-third of my property between Zayd and Amr,' and Amr is dead, Zayd gets half the third because the import of this expression is that each of them gets one-third, unlike the previous. Do you not see that one who says: 'One-third of my property to so-and-so' and is silent, he gets the entire third, but if he says: 'One-third of my property between so-and-so' and is silent, he does not get the entire third but half of it.
Source pages p. 484

Commentary
This passage distinguishes between two expressions. When the testator says 'to Zayd and Amr' (using 'and'), if one is dead, the other gets the whole, as in the previous lesson. But when he says 'between Zayd and Amr' (using 'between'), the word 'between' implies division, so each is entitled to half of the bequeathed third. Therefore, if Amr is dead, Zayd gets only half of the third, and the other half returns to the testator's heirs. The passage illustrates with an example: saying 'one-third to so-and-so' gives the whole, but 'between so-and-so' gives half.

Key Terms
بين (bayna): Between; implies division among the named parties

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
If a testator says 'I bequeath one-third of my property between Zayd and Amr,' and Amr dies before the testator, what does Zayd receive?
A) One-third of the estate
B) One-sixth of the estate
C) One-third of the bequeathed third
D) Half of the bequeathed third

Key Takeaway
When a testator uses 'between', the bequest is divided equally among the named, and if one predeceases, the survivor gets only his share.

Bequest When Testator Has No Property at Time of Bequest
Ruling on bequest with no property at time of bequest

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi ruling on bequest when the testator’s property changes between bequest and death, distinguishing between a bequest of a general share and a bequest of a specific object or type.

Core Idea
A bequest is valid even if the testator owns nothing at the time, as long as property exists at death.

This lesson addresses a common concern: what happens if someone bequeaths one-third of his property but has no property at the moment of the bequest? How does the Hanafi school handle property acquired later? We will explore the underlying principle that a bequest is a contract attached to after death, and we will distinguish between a bequest of a general share (like one-third of his property) and a bequest of a specific object or type (like a particular sheep or one-third of his flock).

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is a bequest (wasiyya) of one-third of the testator's property. The ruling is that it is valid even if the testator had no property at the time of the bequest, provided he owns property at death. The legatee receives one-third of whatever property exists at death.
The ruling is from Kanz al-Daqaiq and is presented as the correct view in the Hanafi school.
2
Trace the legal reasoning (ta'lil)
The passage explains that a bequest is a contract of substitution (istikhlaf) attached to after death (mudaf ila ma ba'd al-mawt). Its ruling is established after death, so only property existing at death matters. This is the key principle.
The phrase 'عقد استخلاف مضاف إلى ما بعد الموت' is the core ta'lil.
3
Distinguish the two scenarios
First scenario: bequest of a general share (e.g., 'one-third of my property'). This is valid even if the testator had no property at the time, because the bequest attaches to whatever property exists at death. Second scenario: bequest of a specific object or type (e.g., 'one-third of my sheep' or 'this specific sheep'). If that object or entire type perishes before death, the bequest becomes void; even if he later acquires other sheep or objects, the legatee's right does not transfer to the new property.
The key distinction: general share attaches to the estate as it exists at death; specific object/type attaches to that particular object.
4
Apply to a case of later acquisition
If the testator had no sheep at the time of bequest but later acquired sheep and then died, the bequest of 'one-third of his sheep' is valid because the bequest attaches to the type, and the type existed at death. The passage states that the correct view (al-sahih) is that it is valid, analogizing from the case of a general bequest.
This is an important practical scenario: the bequest is valid even though no sheep existed at the time of bequest.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وبثلثه له ولا مال له له ثلث ما يملكه عند موته لأن الوصية عقد استخلاف مضاف إلى ما بعد الموت، ويثبت حكمه بعده، فيشترط وجود المال عند الموت، سواء اكتسبه بعد الوصية أو قبلها بعد أن لم يكن الموصى به عينا أو نوعا معينا، وأما إذا أوصى بعين أو بنوع من ماله كثلث غنمه، فهلكت قبل موته فتبطل الوصية؛ لأنه تعلقت بالعين، فتبطل بفواتها قبل الموت حتى لو اكتسب غنما أخرى أو عينا أخرى بعد ذلك لا يتعلق حق الموصى له بذلك، وإن لم يكن له غنم عند الوصية فاستفادها ثم مات فالصحيح أن الوصية تصح؛ لأنها لو كانت بلفظ المال تصح، فكذا إذا كانت بلفظ نوعه؛ لأن المعتبر وجوده عند الموت لا غير تكملة البحر الرائق: ٢٩٩/٩
And [if he bequeaths] his third to a person and he has no property, he gets a third of whatever he owns at his death because the bequest is a contract of substitution (istikhlaf) attached to after death, and its ruling is established after it. So the existence of property at death is required, whether he acquired it after the bequest or before, as long as the bequeathed item was not a specific object or type. But if he bequeaths a specific object or a type of his property like one-third of his sheep, and they perish before his death, the bequest becomes void because it was attached to the specific object, so it becomes void with its loss before death. Even if he later acquires other sheep or other objects, the legatee's right does not attach to them. And if he had no sheep at the time of bequest and later acquired them and then died, the correct view is that the bequest is valid because if it would be valid with the word 'property' (mal), then likewise with the word 'type,' because what matters is its existence at death and nothing else.
Source pages p. 485

Commentary
This passage explains the ruling when a testator bequeaths one-third to a person but has no property at the time of the bequest. The ruling is that the legatee gets one-third of whatever property the testator owns at death, because a bequest is a contract that takes effect after death, so only property existing at death matters. However, if the testator bequeaths a specific object (like a particular sheep) or a type (like one-third of his flock), and that object perishes before death, the bequest is void. But if he had no sheep at the time of bequest and later acquires a flock, the bequest is valid because the bequest attaches to the type, not to the specific animal.

Key Terms
استخلاف (istikhlaf): Contract of substitution; the legatee succeeds to property after death
عين (ayn): Specific object or property
نوع (naw'): Type or category of property (e.g., sheep)

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
If someone bequeaths one-third of his property to Zayd, but at the time of bequest he has no property, and later he earns 300 dirhams and dies, what does Zayd receive?
A) Nothing, because the bequest was void at the time
B) 100 dirhams
C) 150 dirhams
D) 300 dirhams

Key Takeaway
A bequest is valid even if the testator owned nothing at the time, as long as property exists at death; however, a bequest of a specific object that perishes before death becomes void.

Bequest to Ummahat Awlad and the Poor/Needy: The Minimum of the Plural
Intra-Hanafi dispute on division of a bequest among ummahat awlad, fuqara, and masakin.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the positions of Abu Hanifa/Abu Yusuf and Imam Muhammad regarding the minimum representation of plural nouns in bequests, and apply the Hanafi rule of taking the minimum of one for the definite plural.

Core Idea
In bequests, the definite plural 'al-fuqara' takes a minimum of one, not two — a linguistic principle that divides the third into five shares.

This passage presents a nuanced intra-Hanafi dispute about how to interpret plural terms in a bequest. When a testator leaves one-third to 'the poor' and 'the needy' along with three named ummahat awlad, the key question is: how many individuals does each plural category represent? The answer determines the division of the third into shares. Understanding this dispute illuminates broader Hanafi principles of linguistic interpretation and the hierarchy of proofs within the school.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi position (the two)
Identify the view of Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf: the definite plural takes the minimum of one, so poor and needy each get one share. The third is divided into five shares (three for mothers, one each for poor/needy).
2
Identify the opponent and his view
State Imam Muhammad's position: the plural in bequest requires a minimum of two each, analogizing to inheritance law. This yields seven shares (three for mothers, two each for poor/needy).
3
Analyze the opponent's proof
Understand Muhammad's dalil: bequest is the sister of inheritance, and in inheritance the minimum plural is two. Therefore the same rule applies here.
This is a qiyas argument.
4
Analyze the Hanafi response
The two counter that a definite plural (al-fuqara) is like a definite singular (al-rajul) — both indicate the genus and the minimum is one. They cite the example of oaths: swearing not to buy 'slaves' is broken by buying one slave.
Linguistic principle overrides analogy to inheritance.
5
Determine the practical difference
The thamarah al-khilaf is the number of shares: 5 vs 7. The testator's intent and the actual distribution to recipients differ.
The mufta bihi is the view of the two, dividing into five shares.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وبثلثه لأمهات أولاده، وهن ثلاث وللفقراء والمساكين، لهن ثلاثة من خمسة أسهم أي يقسم الثلث على خمسة أسهم ثلاثة منها لأمهات الأولاد، وسهم للفقراء، وسهم للمساكين، وهذا عندهما، وعند محمد: يقسم على سبعة أسهم للفقراء سهمان وللمساكين سهمان، ولهن ثلاثة أسهم؛ لأن المذكور في الفقراء والمساكين لفظ الجمع، وأدناه في الميراث اثنان والوصية أخت الميراث، وأمهات الأولاد ثلاثة، فكان المجموع سبعة، فيقسم أسباعا، ولهما: أن اسم الجنس المحلى بالألف واللام يتناول الأدنى احتمال الكل كالمفرد المحلى بهما؛ لأنه يراد بهما الجنس إذا لم يكن معهودا، ولا يحتمل ما بينهما، فيتعين الأدنى لتعذر إرادة الكل، ولهذا لو حلف لا يشتري العبيد يحنث بالواحد فيتناول من كل فريق واحد، وأمهات الأولاد ثلاثة، فبلغ السهام خمسة (عيني، فتح وغيرهما بزيادة توضيح)
And [if he bequeaths] his third to the mothers of his children (ummahat awlad), and they are three, and to the poor (fuqara) and the needy (masakin), they (the mothers) get three out of five shares. That is, the third is divided into five shares: three for the ummahat awlad, one for the poor, one for the needy. This is according to the two (Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf). According to Muhammad, it is divided into seven shares: two for the poor, two for the needy, and three for them, because the mention of poor and needy is in the plural form, and the minimum in inheritance is two, and bequest is the sister of inheritance. And the ummahat awlad are three, so the total is seven, so it is divided into sevenths. According to the two (Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf), the generic noun with the definite article (al- and lam) takes the minimum, potentially the whole, like the singular with the definite article, because it denotes the genus when not specified, and it does not include what is between, so the minimum is determined because the whole cannot be intended. Hence, if someone swears not to buy slaves, he breaks the oath with one, so it takes one from each category. The ummahat awlad are three, so the shares amount to five.
Source pages p. 485

Commentary
This passage presents a dispute between Imam Muhammad and the two (Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf) regarding the division of a bequest of one-third to three ummahat awlad (mothers of the testator's children) and to the poor and needy. According to the two, the poor and needy each receive one share, for a total of five shares (three for the mothers, one for poor, one for needy). According to Muhammad, because 'poor' and 'needy' are plural, the minimum for each is two, so there should be two shares for poor and two for needy, total seven shares. The reasoning of the two is that the definite plural (al-fuqara) takes the minimum of one, as in oaths; Muhammad analogizes to inheritance where the minimum plural is two.

Key Terms
أمهات الأولاد (ummahat al-awlad): Mothers of the testator's children (concubines who bore his children)
فقراء (fuqara): The poor; a category of recipients of charity

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf, how many shares do the poor and needy receive when the bequest is to three ummahat awlad, the poor, and the needy?
A) One share each
B) Two shares each
C) One share total
D) Three shares total

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school holds that a definite plural in a bequest is interpreted as a minimum of one individual, leading to a five-share division in this case.

Bequest to Zayd and the Poor: The Intramadhab Dispute
Ruling on bequest to Zayd and the poor, intra-Hanafi dispute

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi positions on dividing a bequest between a named individual and the poor, and explain how the linguistic interpretation of 'plural' drives the ikhtilaf.

Core Idea
The division of a bequest between Zayd and the poor depends on whether 'al-masakin' means at least one or at least two.

A testator bequeaths one-third of his estate to 'Zayd and the poor'. How is that third divided among them? The Hanafi school is unanimous on the validity of the bequest, but disagrees on the shares. This lesson unpacks the reasoning of Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf against that of Imam Muhammad, rooted in a linguistic usul question: what is the minimum count of a definite plural?

Guided Path
1
State the ruling of Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf
Identify the share each party receives according to the two imams.
Zayd gets half, the poor get half.
2
State the ruling of Imam Muhammad
Identify how Muhammad divides the same bequest.
Zayd gets one-third, the poor get two-thirds.
3
Locate the linguistic pivot
The dispute turns on the minimum number implied by the definite plural 'al-masakin'. For the two, it is one; for Muhammad, it is two.
This is a usul al-fiqh principle: whether al-amm (definite plural) indicates one or more.
4
Apply the principle to the bequest
If poor means one, then recipient count is two (Zayd + one poor), so equal halves. If poor means two, then total three recipients, so Zayd gets one-third, each poor gets one-third.
5
Note the thamarah al-khilaf and extend to a solo bequest to the poor
The practical difference: Zayd's share is either half or one-third. Also, a general bequest to the poor can go to one person according to the two, but requires two according to Muhammad.
The passage also states that if the testator points to a specific group, all agree it cannot be given to one person.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وبثلثه لزيد وللمساكين لزيد نصفه، ولهم نصفه أي وإن أوصى أي نصف الثلث للمساكين وعند محمد: ثلثه لزيد، وثلثاه للمساكين، وقد بينا مأخذ كل واحد من الفريقين، ولو أوصى بثلث ماله للمساكين، له صرفه إلى مسكين واحد عندهما، وعند محمد: لا يصرف إلا إلى مسكينين، والخلاف فيما إذا لم يشر إلى مساكين؛ إذ لو أشار إلى جماعة وقال: ثلث مالي لهذه المساكين لا يجوز صرفه إلى واحد اتفاقا.
And [if he bequeaths] his third to Zayd and the poor, Zayd gets half of it, and they get half of it. That is, if he bequeaths half of the third to the poor. According to Muhammad: one-third to Zayd, two-thirds to the poor. And we have explained the basis of each of the two groups. And if he bequeaths a third of his property to the poor, he may give it to one poor person according to the two (Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf). According to Muhammad, it may only be given to two poor persons. And the dispute is when he did not point to specific poor people; if he pointed to a group and said: 'One-third of my property to these poor people,' it is not permissible to give it to one person by agreement.
Source pages p. 485

Commentary
This passage gives a second dispute regarding division when the bequest is to Zayd and the poor. The ruling of the two (Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf) is that Zayd gets half the third and the poor get the other half. But Muhammad holds that Zayd gets one-third and the poor get two-thirds. The basis is their differing views on the minimum number represented by 'the poor' (masakin): for the two, it is one; for Muhammad, it is two. The passage also extends to a bequest solely to the poor: the two allow giving to one poor person, Muhammad requires two, unless the testator specified a particular group.

Key Terms
مساكين (masakin): The needy; a category of recipients in a bequest.
ثلث (thuluth): One-third of the estate, the maximum allowed for bequests to non-heirs.

Key Terms from Source Passage

A) One-fourth
B) One-third
C) One-half
D) Two-thirds

Key Takeaway
The division of a bequest to a named individual and the poor depends on the minimum number implied by 'the poor' – a linguistic usul question that splits the Hanafi school.

Bequest of Specific Amounts and Including a Third as Partner
Ruling on partnership in bequests with fixed sums.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to calculate the shares in a bequest when a third party is made a partner in two equal bequests.

Core Idea
Including a third as partner divides each bequest equally among all.

A testator bequeaths 100 dirhams to each of two people. Later, he says to a third: 'I have made you a partner with them.' How should the third's share be calculated? This lesson clarifies that the third becomes an equal partner in each bequest individually, not merely in the total sum. The principle is that 'ishrak (making a partner) creates equal sharing in each specific bequest unless the testator specifies otherwise.

Guided Path
1
Identify the original bequests
Note that the testator gave 100 dirhams to each of two persons. They are separate bequests, not a single joint bequest.
Each bequest is independent.
2
Interpret the declaration of partnership
The testator says to a third person: 'I have made you a partner with them.' This creates a share for the third in each of the two original bequests.
The pronoun 'them' refers to both original legatees.
3
Determine the third's share in each bequest
Since the third is made a partner, he gets an equal share with each original legatee in their respective bequest. Thus, from the first 100 he gets one-third, from the second 100 he gets another one-third.
The third becomes a co-legatee in both.
4
Calculate the final amounts for all
Each of the three now gets the same amount: 66.66 dirhams (one-third of each 100, total 200/3).
The total bequest remains 200 dirhams, split equally.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وبمائة لرجل وبمائة لآخر، فقال لآخر: أشركتك معهما، له ثلث كل مائة، فيكون ستة وستون وثلثا درهم ولكل واحد منهما كذلك؛ لأن نصيبهما متساو، وقد أشرك آخر معهما، فيكون شريكا لكل منهما، فله ثلث ما لكل منهما (ملا مسكين، فتح وغيرهما)
And [if he bequeaths] one hundred dirhams to a man and one hundred to another, then he said to a third: 'I have made you a partner with them,' he gets one-third of each hundred, so it becomes sixty-six and two-thirds dirhams, and each of the other two likewise, because their shares were equal, and he made a third a partner with them, so he is a partner with each of them, so he gets one-third of what each has.
Source pages p. 485

Commentary
This passage deals with a scenario where a testator bequeaths 100 dirhams to each of two people, and then later says to a third person: 'I have made you a partner with them.' The ruling is that the third person becomes a partner in each bequest, so he gets one-third of each 100, i.e., 33.33 from each, totaling 66.66. Consequently, each of the original two also gets 66.66, because their shares are reduced by the share given to the third. This is based on equal partnership.

Key Terms
أشرك (ashraka): He made [someone] a partner; to include as a co-legatee

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) 33.33 dirhams
B) 50 dirhams
C) 66.66 dirhams
D) 100 dirhams

Key Takeaway
When a testator makes a third a partner in two equal bequests, the third receives one-third from each, resulting in equal shares for all three legatees.

Calculating Shares When a Partner Is Included in Unequal Bequests
Ruling on calculating shares with a partner in unequal bequests

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to calculate the share of a partner included in unequal bequests and explain the Hanafi principle of proportional sharing.

Core Idea
A partner in a bequest shares proportionally in each bequest, not in the total sum.

When a testator makes unequal bequests to two persons and then includes a third as a partner, how is the third's share determined? This passage illustrates the Hanafi rule that the partner shares in each bequest proportionally, not in the combined total. Understanding this calculation is essential for drafting wills that maintain the testator's intended distribution.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two original bequests
Note the amounts bequeathed to each of the first two beneficiaries: 400 to one, 200 to the other.
2
Recognize the effect of ishrak
When the testator says 'I have made you a partner with them,' the third becomes a partner in each bequest equally, not in the total pot.
Ishrak creates a separate sharing in each distinct bequest.
3
Calculate the third's share from each bequest
Take one-third of each original bequest: from 400, one-third is 133.33; from 200, one-third is 66.67.
One-third is used because there are now three parties sharing each bequest equally.
4
Sum the shares to get total
Add the two amounts: 133.33 + 66.67 = 200. The third partner receives 200 in total.
5
Determine the reduced shares of the original beneficiaries
Subtract the third's portion from each: the first original gets 400 - 133.33 = 266.67; the second gets 200 - 66.67 = 133.33.
The original ratio of 2:1 is preserved (266.67 : 133.33 = 2:1).

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وبأربع مائة له، وبمائتين لآخر، فقال لآخر: أشركتك معهما، له ثلث كل مائة فيكون له من الأول مائة وثلاثة وثلاثون وثلث ومن الثاني ستة وستون وثلثان فله مائتان بالتمام، وهذا لأن نصيب كل واحد منهما كان مختلفا، وبالإشراك صار شريكا لكل منهما في نصيبه أثلاثا.
And [if he bequeaths] four hundred to one person and two hundred to another, then he said to a third: 'I have made you a partner with them,' he gets one-third of each hundred, so he gets from the first one hundred and thirty-three and one-third, and from the second sixty-six and two-thirds, so he gets two hundred in total. This is because the share of each was different, and by making a partner, he becomes a partner with each in his share by thirds.
Source pages p. 485

Commentary
This passage extends the previous ruling to unequal bequests: one person gets 400, another gets 200. When a third is made a partner, he gets one-third of each bequest: from the first, he gets one-third of 400 (133.33), from the second, one-third of 200 (66.67), totaling 200. The original two then have their shares reduced accordingly: the first gets 266.67, the second gets 133.33.

Key Terms
إشراك (ishrak): Inclusion as a partner in a bequest, creating a proportionate sharing in each specific bequest.
أثلاثا (athlathan): By thirds; indicating that the partner shares equally with the original beneficiary in each bequest, dividing it into three parts of which the partner gets one.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
A testator bequeaths 400 dirhams to A and 200 dirhams to B, then makes C a partner with them. How much does C receive?
A) 133.33 dirhams
B) 200 dirhams
C) 300 dirhams
D) 66.67 dirhams

Key Takeaway
When a testator includes a third partner in unequal bequests, the partner shares proportionally in each bequest, preserving the original ratio between the original beneficiaries.

Garment Bequest Distribution When One Garment Is Lost
Explains the distribution rule when one of three bequeathed garments is lost

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi rule for distributing bequeathed garments when one is lost and explain the rationale based on taraddud al-haqq (uncertainty of right).

Core Idea
When a specific bequest item is lost, the remaining legatees share proportionally due to uncertainty.

This lesson examines a specific ruling from Kanz al-Daqaiq regarding a bequest of three garments of varying quality. When the finest garment is lost before delivery, the shares of the remaining two legatees become uncertain, and the Hanafi school prescribes a rule to resolve this uncertainty equitably. The commentary from Fath al-Qadir clarifies the reasoning using the concept of taraddud al-haqq.

Guided Path
1
Identify the scenario and base shares
The testator bequeaths three specific garments: worn-out, medium, and fine. The matn states: 'For the owner of the worn-out, two-thirds; for the owner of the medium, a third each.' Determine what these shares refer to (likely of the total bequest or the remaining garments).
The matn is concise; the share fractions apply when all three are present.
2
Consider the loss of the fine garment
The finest garment is lost (halik). This affects the distribution because the fine garment's legatee now has a claim on the survivors, but his specific item is gone.
The loss creates a situation of uncertainty: we don't know if the lost garment was better or worse than the survivors.
3
Understand the uncertainty (taraddud)
The commentary explains that if the lost garment was of higher quality than the two survivors, the legatee's right is in the better of the two; if lower, in the inferior. Since we cannot know which, his right is uncertain between the two survivors.
This uncertainty (taraddud al-haqq) is the key legal cause for the ruling.
4
Apply the rule: proportional share from each survivor
Because the right is uncertain, the legatee takes from each of the two remaining garments two-thirds of its value. This is 'what remains after the other two have taken', suggesting a compensatory mechanism.
The phrase 'two-thirds from each' may mean two-thirds of the value of each surviving garment.
5
Note the authority level and ambiguity
This ruling is from Zahir al-Riwayah via Fath al-Qadir, but the text has OCR issues. The exact arithmetic is debated among later commentators.
Review reason: The commentary's logic is unclear and may contain OCR errors.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ولذي الردى ثلثاه ولذي الوسط ثلث كل أي لصاحب الثوب الردى ولذي الوسط إلخ لأن الهالك إن كان أرفع هذين الباقيين كان حقه في الجيد منهما، وإن كان أردأ، كان حقه في الرديء منهما، فتردد حقه بينهما، فأخذ من كل منهما ثلثا، وهو الباقي بعد أخذ الآخرين. (فتح)
And for the owner of the worn-out garment, two-thirds; and for the owner of the medium garment, a third each; meaning: for the owner of the worn-out garment, etc. Because if the lost one is of higher quality than these two remaining, his right is in the better of the two; and if it is of lower quality, his right is in the inferior of the two. So his right is uncertain between them, so he takes from each of them two-thirds, which is what remains after the other two have taken.
Source pages p. 488

Commentary
This passage from the matn of Kanz al-Daqaiq states a ruling about a bequest of three specific garments: one worn-out, one medium, and one presumably fine. The matn gives shares: the legatee of the worn-out garment gets two-thirds, and the legatee of the medium garment gets one-third of the total. The commentary explains the case where the finest garment is lost. The right of the two remaining legatees becomes uncertain: if the lost garment was better than both, the legatee of the worn-out (or the remaining two) gets only the better of the two surviving; if the lost was worse, he gets the inferior. Since the right is uncertain between the two survivors, each takes two-thirds of what remains after the other two (i.e., after the lost one and one other?) Actually, the text says 'he takes from each of them two-thirds', meaning the legatee with uncertain right takes two-thirds from each of the remaining two garments? This is ambiguous. The reference '(فتح)' indicates the commentary is from Fath al-Qadir. Overall, the ruling ensures equitable distribution when the object of bequest is partially lost.

Key Terms
الردى (al-rada): Worn-out or low-quality garment
الوسط (al-wasat): Medium-quality garment
الهالك (al-halik): The lost or destroyed item (the finest garment in this context)
التردد (al-taraddud): Uncertainty; the state of the right being indeterminate between two possibilities

A) The loss of any garment
B) The uncertainty of the right between the two survivors
C) The higher quality of the lost garment
D) The bequest being from a specific category

Key Takeaway
When a specific bequest item is lost, the Hanafi school resolves uncertainty by giving the legatee a proportional share from each surviving item.
