Conditions for Bequest to Relatives and Distribution Among Uncles
Explains Abu Hanifa's six conditions and the dispute with Sahibayn on distribution to uncles.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state Abu Hanifa's six conditions for a valid bequest to relatives and apply them to determine the correct distribution, distinguishing the view of the Sahibayn.

Core Idea
A bequest to 'relatives' is valid only under six conditions; distribution depends on whether closeness is considered.

This lesson examines the Hanafi rulings on bequests to relatives (al-wasiyya li'l-aqarib). The passage from Kanz al-Daqa'iq outlines six conditions set by Abu Hanifa and applies them to scenarios involving paternal and maternal uncles. It also highlights the significant intra-madhhab dispute with the Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani) regarding the role of closeness in distribution. By the end, you will be able to trace the practical implications of these differing views.

Guided Path
1
List Abu Hanifa's six conditions
Identify the six requirements from the passage: mahram relationship, equal treatment of paternal/maternal, non-inheritor, precedence of nearest, at least two beneficiaries, and exclusion of parents/children.
These conditions are found in the early part of the commentary.
2
Understand the plural requirement
The word 'aqarib' (and similar plurals) requires at least two recipients. If only one relative exists, he receives only half, with the other half returning to the heirs.
This is a key difference from a singular expression like 'dhi qarabatihi' which allows one.
3
Compare the two illustrative cases
Examine the two scenarios: (a) two paternal uncles and two maternal uncles; (b) one paternal uncle and two maternal uncles. Determine the distribution under Abu Hanifa (closeness considered) and under the Sahibayn (no closeness).
In case (a), Abu Hanifa gives all to the two paternal uncles; Sahibayn give each of the four a quarter. In case (b), Abu Hanifa gives half to the paternal uncle, half to the two maternal; Sahibayn give a third to paternal, two-thirds to maternal.
4
Analyze the mahram condition dispute
Note that Abu Hanifa voids the bequest if no mahram relative exists. The Sahibayn do not void it; they distribute among the relatives present.
This shows that the Sahibayn do not consider mahram a condition.
5
Apply to a new scenario
Given a testator with one paternal uncle and one maternal aunt, decide distribution under Abu Hanifa and Sahibayn.
According to the passage, they share equally under Abu Hanifa because both are equally close; the Sahibayn would also share equally (no closeness).

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الوصية للأقارب وغيرهم
فصاعدا، فإن كان له عمان وخالان فهي لعميه ولو عم وخالان له النصف ولهما النصف، ولو له عم وعمة استويا ولولد فلان للذكر والأنثى على السواء،
لا يعتبر الجمع اتفاقا، كذا في "الفتح"، قال في "الكفاية": حاصله : عند أبي حنيفة حللته في هذه المسألة ستة أشياء: أحدها: أن يكون المستحق بهذا اللفظ ذا رحم محرم من الموصي، والثاني: أن ذلك لا يتفاوت من قبل الآباء والأمهات، والثالث: يجب أن يكون ممن لا يرثه والرابع: أن يقدم الأقرب والخامس: أن يكون المستحق اثنين فصاعدا، والسادس: أن لا يدخل فيه الوالد والولد ويدخل فيه الجد وولد الولد في ظاهر الرواية، وروى الحسن عن أبي حنيفة، وهلال عن أبي يوسف له: أنه لا يدخل. فصاعدا منصوب على الحال من مقدر تقديره فمضى الحكم صاعدا (عيني) فإن كان إلخ: تفريع على ما بين من أن الوصية في الصورة المذكورة تكون للأقرب فالأقرب وتكون للاثنين فصاعدا، وإشارة إلى مظهر الخلاف يعني إن كان للشخص الذي أوصى لأقاربه أو لذي قرابته أو لأرحامه أو لأنسابه عمان وخالان، فالوصية لعميه أي لعمي ذلك الشخص؛ لأنهما أقرب كما في الإرث، ولفظ الجمع يراد به المثنى في الوصية على ما بيناه، فيكتفى بهما، هذا عند أبي حنيفة، وعندهما يكون بينهم أرباعا ؛ لأنهما لا يعتبران الأقرب. (عيني بزيادة من المحشي) ولو عم وخالان إلخ أي لو كان لذلك الشخص في الصورة المذكورة عم وخالان كان للعم نصف الموصى به، وللخالين النصف الآخر؛ لأن اللفظ جمع، فلابد من اعتبار معنى الجمع فيه وهو الاثنان في الوصية على ما عرف، فيضم إلى العم الخالان؛ ليصير جمعا، فيأخذ هو النصف؛ لأنه أقرب، ويأخذان النصف؛ لعدم من يتقدم عليهما فيه، بخلاف ما إذا أوصى لذي قرابته حيث يكون جميع الوصية للعم؛ لأن اللفظ مفرد، فيجوز للواحد جميع الوصية؛ إذ هو الأقرب، وهذا عند أبي حنيفة، وقالا تكون الوصية أثلاثا ثلث للعم وثلثان للخالين؛ لعدم اعتبار الأقربية عندهما، ولو كان له واحد لا غير كان له النصف؛ لما بينا أنه لابد من اعتبار معنى الجمع فيه، ويرد النصف إلى الورثة. [ رمز الحقائق ٤٨٨/٢] (طائي بزيادة يسيره) استويا: لأن قرابتهما مستويان، ومعنى الجمع قد تحقق بهما، فاستحقا، حتى لو كان له أخوال معهما لا يستحقون شيئا؛ لأنهما أقرب، ولا حاجة إلى الضم إليهما؛ لكمال النصاب بهما، ولو انعدم المحرم بطلت الوصية؛ لأنها متقيدة بهذا، وهذا كله عند أبي حنيفة، وعندهما لا تبطل ولا تختص الأعمام بالوصية دون الأخوال؛ لما عرف من مذهبهما
The chapter of bequests. Bequest to relatives and others. Continuing with the above... If the testator has two paternal uncles and two maternal uncles, the bequest is for his two paternal uncles. And if he has one paternal uncle and two maternal uncles, he (the paternal uncle) gets half and they (the two maternal uncles) get half. And if he has a paternal uncle and a maternal aunt, they are equal. And for the children of so-and-so, male and female are equal. The plural is not considered by agreement? Thus in al-Fath. He said in al-Kifayah: In summary, according to Abu Hanifa, six matters are required in this issue: First, that the entitled person by this expression be a mahram relative of the testator. Second, that there is no difference between paternal and maternal sides. Third, that the person must not be an inheritor from the testator. Fourth, that the nearest be given precedence. Fifth, that the entitled persons be two or more. Sixth, that the parent and child are not included, but the grandfather and grandchild are included in the apparent narration. And al-Hasan reported from Abu Hanifa, and Hilal from Abu Yusuf, that they are not included. 'Fasa'idan' (and upwards) is in the accusative as a circumstantial accusative from an implied estimation: 'So the ruling continues upward'. (Ayni) 'If he has...' etc.: a branch on what has been explained that the bequest in the mentioned scenario is for the nearest, and for two or more. And an indication of the point of difference: meaning if the person who bequeathed to his relatives or his kinsmen or his womb relatives or his lineage has two paternal and two maternal uncles, the bequest is for his two paternal uncles, because they are nearer as in inheritance, and the plural expression is intended to mean the dual in bequest as we explained, so they suffice. This is according to Abu Hanifa. According to them (the two companions), it is divided into fourths among them, because they do not consider closeness. (Ayni with addition from the commentator) 'And if one paternal uncle and two maternal uncles...' i.e., if that person in the mentioned scenario has one paternal uncle and two maternal uncles, the paternal uncle gets half of the bequeathed property, and the two maternal uncles get the other half, because the expression is plural, so the meaning of plural must be considered, which is two in bequest as known. Thus the two maternal uncles are joined to the paternal uncle to make a plural, so he takes half because he is nearer, and they take half because there is no one before them. Unlike if he bequeathed to 'his kinsman' (singular), where all the bequest goes to the paternal uncle, because the expression is singular, so one person can take all the bequest, since he is the nearest. This is according to Abu Hanifa. They (the two companions) say the bequest is divided into thirds: one third for the paternal uncle and two thirds for the two maternal uncles, because they do not consider closeness. And if he has only one (relative) not more, he gets half, because we have explained that the meaning of plural must be considered, and the other half is returned to the heirs. [Ramz al-Haqa'iq 2/488] (Tai with slight addition) 'They are equal': because their kinship is equal, and the meaning of plural is realized by them, so they become entitled. Even if there are maternal uncles with them, they do not get anything, because they (the paternal uncle and maternal aunt) are closer, and there is no need to join others because the required number (two) is complete with them. If the mahram condition is not met, the bequest becomes void, because it is conditional upon this. All this according to Abu Hanifa. According to them, it does not become void, and the paternal uncles are not exclusively entitled over the maternal uncles, as known from their madhhab.
Source pages p. 497

Commentary
This passage is an intra-Hanafi dispute commentary on bequests to relatives. The commentator from Kanz al-Daqa'iq explains the matn's rulings. First, he enumerates Abu Hanifa's six conditions for a bequest to relatives to be valid: the beneficiary must be a mahram relative (i.e., a marriage-prohibited relative, such as uncle, aunt, grandparent, grandchild, but not sibling? Actually mahram includes many), the relative's connection is equal on both paternal and maternal sides (so no preference by lineage), the beneficiary must not be an inheritor from the testator (so that the bequest does not interfere with inheritance rights), the nearest relative is given precedence, there must be at least two beneficiaries (since the phrase 'aqarib is a plural requiring at least two), and parents and children are excluded (but grandparents and grandchildren are included in the apparent narration, though al-Hasan and Hilal narrate exclusion from Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf respectively).

Then the commentary applies these rules to the matn's cases. If the testator has two paternal uncles and two maternal uncles, Abu Hanifa gives the entire bequest to the two paternal uncles because they are closer (paternal uncles are considered nearer than maternal in Hanafi thought? Actually the principle applied is that in inheritance, closer relatives exclude farther ones, and here paternal uncles are considered closer than maternal uncles? The text says 'as in inheritance' which suggests that in inheritance, paternal uncles have precedence over maternal uncles? But this is not exactly inheritance, it's bequest. The reasoning is that the plural expression 'aqarib requires at least two beneficiaries, and the closest two are the paternal uncles. The Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) do not consider closeness, so they divide the bequest equally among all four uncles (each gets one fourth).

In the second case, one paternal uncle and two maternal uncles: Abu Hanifa gives half to the paternal uncle (being nearer) and half to the two maternal uncles (they share half). The Sahibayn give one third to the paternal uncle and two thirds to the two maternal uncles (each maternal uncle gets one third).

In the third case, a paternal uncle and a maternal aunt: since both are close and together form a plural (two persons), they split the bequest equally. No further joining of others is needed. If the mahram condition is absent, the bequest becomes void according to Abu Hanifa, but the Sahibayn do not void it.

Finally, if there is only one relative (e.g., only one maternal uncle), he gets only half of the bequeathed property, because the plural expression requires at least two, and since there is only one, the other half reverts to the testator's heirs.

Key Terms
أقارب (aqaarib): Relatives; the beneficiaries of a bequest when the testator says 'to my relatives' or similar.
ذو رحم محرم (dhu rahm muhrim): A relative whom one is permanently prohibited from marrying (mahram), e.g., uncle, aunt, grandparent, grandchild.
الجمع (al-jam'): Plural form; in bequest, the plural (like 'aqarib' or 'awlad') requires at least two beneficiaries (al-muthanna is considered plural in this context).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to Abu Hanifa, if a person makes a bequest to his 'aqarib' (relatives) and he has only one maternal uncle, how much does the maternal uncle receive?
A) The entire bequeathed property
B) Half of the bequeathed property
C) One third of the bequeathed property
D) Nothing, the bequest is void

Key Takeaway
Abu Hanifa's six conditions and the dispute with Sahibayn on closeness and mahram significantly affect how a bequest to relatives is distributed.

Bequest to 'Children of So-and-So': Equality and the Effect of Plurality
Ruling with proof: linguistic analysis and intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish between a bequest to 'walad' (singular) and 'awlad' (plural) and state the distribution rules for each case.

Core Idea
In Hanafi law, 'awlad' (plural) requires at least two beneficiaries, so a single child receives only half the bequest.

This lesson examines a bequest where the testator says 'to the children of so-and-so' (awlad). The Hanafi school holds that distribution among them is equal, regardless of gender. However, the key nuance lies in the linguistic difference between 'walad' (singular) and 'awlad' (plural), which affects the share when there is only one beneficiary. We will also explore the inclusive scope of 'awlad' regarding grandchildren.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two expressions
Recognize that the text distinguishes between 'walad' (singular, ism jins) and 'awlad' (plural, jam'). Understand that each carries different implications for distribution.
2
State the base rule for 'awlad'
For a bequest to 'awlad', the ruling is that males and females share equally. This is agreed upon according to the source.
The commentary in al-Kifayah confirms this even if all beneficiaries are female.
3
Contrast with 'walad' singular
If the testator says 'to the child of so-and-so' (walad), and there is only one child, that child receives the entire bequeathed one-third. If he says 'to the children' (awlad) and only one child exists, that child gets only half of the one-third (one-sixth of estate).
Reason: 'awlad' is plural requiring at least two; the single child takes half, the other half reverts to heirs.
4
Understand the linguistic basis
The term 'walad' is a generic noun (ism jins) that applies to the minimum individual, whereas 'awlad' is a true plural (jam'). The minimum plural in bequest and inheritance is two, by Hanafi rule.
Analogous to bequest to 'aqarib' (relatives): if one paternal uncle, he gets half.
5
Consider inclusion of grandchildren
If the testator bequeaths to 'children of so-and-so' and there are no direct children, children of sons are included. Whether children of daughters are included is subject to two narrations within the Hanafi school.
This is an intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf.

Source Text

لا يعتبر الجمع اتفاقا، كذا في "الفتح"، قال في "الكفاية": حتى لو كانوا ذكورا وإناثا يقسم بينهم بالسوية، ولو كان الكل إناثا دخلن تحت الوصية؛ لأن الوصية =

الوصية للأقارب وغيرهم
ولورثة فلان للذكر مثل حظ الأنثيين.
باسم الولد، واسم الولد يطلق على الإناث حالة الانفراد كما يطلق على الذكور، ثم في مسألتنا إن لم يكن لفلان إلا ولد واحد كان الثلث كله له بخلاف ما لو أوصى لأولاد فلان، وله ولد واحد، فإنه يستحق النصف، ووجه الفرق: أن الأولاد جمع، وأقل الجمع في باب الوصية والميراث اثنان فكان للواحد النصف، كما لو أوصى لأقربائه، وله عم واحد كان له النصف، وأما الولد فليس باسم جمع، فإنما هو اسم جنس، ومطلق اسم الجنس يطلق على أدنى ما يطلق عليه الاسم، كما لو حلف لا يشرب الماء، ولا يتزوج النساء، حيث يحنث بشرب قطرة، ونكاح واحدة، وإذا أوصى لأولاد فلان وليس لفلان أولاد صلبية يدخل في الوصية أولاد البنين، وهل يدخل أولاد البنات؟ فيه روايتان.
للذكر مثل حظ إلخ: يعني لورثة فلان يدفع للذكر قدر حظ الأنثيين؛ لأنه اسم مشتق من الوراثة، وترتب الاسم على المشتق يدل على العلية، ألا ترى أن الله تعالى لما نص على الوراثة بقوله: ﴿وَعَلَى الْوَارِثِ مِثْلُ ذَلِكَ ﴾ (البقرة: (۲۳۳)، ترتب الحكم عليها حتى وجبت النفقة بقدرها، ثم شرط هذه الوصية أن يموت فلان الموصى لورثته قبل موت الموصي، حتى يعرف ورثته منهم حتى لو مات الموصي قبل موت الموصى لورثته، بطلت الوصية، بخلاف ما إذا أوصى لولده ولو كان مع ورثته موصى له آخر قسم بينهم وبينه على الرؤوس، ثم ما أصاب الورثة جمع، وقسم بينهم للذكر مثل حظ الأنثيين تكملة البحر الرائق: ٣٥٥/٩]
And for the children of so-and-so, male and female are equal. The plural is not considered by agreement? Thus in al-Fath. He said in al-Kifayah: Even if they are males and females, it is divided equally among them. And if all are females, they are included in the bequest because the bequest is by the name 'child' (walad), and the name 'child' applies to females in isolation as it applies to males. Then in our issue, if so-and-so does not have except one child, the whole one-third goes to him, unlike if he bequeathed 'to the children of so-and-so' and he has one child, then that child gets half. The distinction is that 'awlad' is a plural, and the minimum plural in the chapter of bequest and inheritance is two, so the single gets half, just as if he bequeathed to his relatives and he has one paternal uncle, that uncle gets half. As for 'walad', it is not a plural form; it is a generic noun, and the absolute generic noun applies to the minimum that the name applies to, like if he swore not to drink water or not to marry women, he breaks the oath with a drop or with marrying one. And if he bequeathed to the children of so-and-so and so-and-so has no direct children, the children of his sons enter the bequest. Whether the children of his daughters enter? There are two narrations. 'For the male the share of two females' i.e., for the heirs of so-and-so, the male gets the share of two females because it is a name derived from inheritance, and the attribution of the name to the derived form indicates causation. Do you not see that Allah explicitly mentioned inheritance in His saying: 'And upon the heir is an obligation like that' (al-Baqarah 2:233), so the ruling is attached to it such that maintenance becomes obligatory according to it. Then the condition of this bequest is that the person (so-and-so) whose heirs are the beneficiaries dies before the testator, so that his heirs are known from him. If the testator dies before the one bequeathed to his heirs, the bequest becomes void. Unlike if he bequeathed to his child. And if there is another legatee along with the heirs, it is divided among them per capita. Then what goes to the heirs is collected and divided among them for the male the share of two females. (Takmilat al-Bahr al-Ra'iq 9/355)
Source pages p. 498

Commentary
This passage continues the discussion on bequests, now focusing on two specific expressions: bequest 'to the children of so-and-so' (awlad) and 'to the heirs of so-and-so' (waratha).

The matn states that for 'awlad', distribution is equal among males and females. The commentary from al-Kifayah clarifies that this holds even if all beneficiaries are female; they are included because the term 'walad' applies to both genders. However, the commentator then contrasts two scenarios: if the testator says 'to the child of so-and-so' (walad, singular), and that person has only one child, that child receives the entire bequeathed one-third. But if the testator says 'to the children of so-and-so' (awlad, plural), and there is only one child, that child gets only half, because the plural requires at least two, so the single child takes half and the other half reverts to heirs. The analogy is made with a bequest to 'aqarib': if there is one paternal uncle, he gets half due to the plural form.

For the expression 'to the heirs of so-and-so', the distribution follows inheritance shares: each male gets twice the share of a female, because the term 'waratha' is derived from 'irth' (inheritance) and the Islamic inheritance law (Quran 2:233) establishes the principle. The commentary adds that this bequest is conditional: the person whose heirs are designated must die before the testator, so that his heirs can be identified. If the testator dies first, the bequest is void because the beneficiaries are uncertain.

Finally, if there are multiple legatees including the heirs, distribution is per capita among all legatees, but within the heir-group, the male-female ratio applies.

Key Terms
أولاد (awlaad): Children (plural); used in bequest to refer to the descendants of a specific person.
الولد (al-walad): Child (singular); a generic noun that includes both male and female offspring.
اسم جنس (ism jins): Generic noun; denotes a category and applies to the smallest instance.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
If a testator says, 'I bequeath one-third of my property to the children of Zaid,' and Zaid has only one son, how much does that son receive?
A) The entire one-third
B) Half of the one-third (one-sixth of the estate)
C) One-third of the one-third (one-ninth of the estate)
D) Nothing, the bequest is void

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi law, a bequest to 'children' (awlad) is distributed equally among all beneficiaries, but the plural form requires at least two; if only one exists, that child gets only half the bequest.

Bequest to 'Heirs of So-and-So': Inheritance-Based Distribution and Conditions
Ruling with proof: Quranic derivation and condition of prior death

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the distribution rule for a bequest to 'heirs of so-and-so' and identify the condition that the designated person must die before the testator.

Core Idea
A bequest to 'heirs of so-and-so' is distributed following inheritance shares, but it only becomes valid if the designated person predeceases the testator.

This lesson covers a bequest where the testator says 'to the heirs of so-and-so'. Unlike the bequest to 'children', this distribution follows the inheritance shares set by Allah: the male receives twice the female's share. The proof is derived from the word 'waratha' itself, which is linked to inheritance (irth) and the Quranic principle. A critical condition is that the person whose heirs are bequeathed must die before the testator, otherwise the bequest is void due to uncertainty.

Guided Path
1
State the ruling for 'waratha'
When a testator bequeaths to 'the heirs of so-and-so', the distribution is based on inheritance shares: each male gets double the share of each female.
2
Identify the Quranic proof
The term 'waratha' is derived from 'irth' (inheritance). Allah says in Quran 2:233: 'And upon the heir is an obligation like that.' This verse is taken to indicate that the ruling on maintenance follows inheritance shares, and by analogy, the bequest to 'waratha' follows the same ratio.
The text says: 'ترتب الاسم على المشتق يدل على العلية' – the attachment of the name to its derivation indicates causation.
3
Note the condition of prior death
The person whose heirs are bequeathed (so-and-so) must die before the testator. Only then can his heirs be identified. If the testator dies first, the bequest is void because the beneficiaries are unknown.
Distinguish from bequest to 'children' where no such condition is needed (children are known regardless of order of death).
4
Understand interaction with other legatees
If there is another legatee alongside the heirs, the bequeathed amount is divided per capita among all legatees first. Then, the portion allocated to the heirs is further subdivided among them based on the male:female ratio.
Example: One-third is bequeathed: half to Zaid (specific legatee) and half to 'heirs of Amr'. The heirs' half is then distributed among Amr's heirs: male double female.

Bequest of Fruit, Wool, and Milk: Existing vs. Future
Explaining when bequest of fruit applies to existing vs future produce

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi rules on bequests of fruit, yield, wool, and milk to determine whether the legatee receives only existing items or also future ones.

Core Idea
In Hanafi bequest law, 'fruit' only covers existing produce unless 'forever' is added; 'yield' inherently includes future.

The Hanafi school distinguishes between different types of bequests based on custom and the wording used. This lesson explains how the terms 'thamar' (fruit) and 'ghallah' (yield) affect the scope of a bequest, and why bequests of wool and milk never include future growth. Understanding these distinctions is crucial for drafting valid wills and interpreting them correctly.

Guided Path
1
Identify the type of bequest
Determine whether the bequest is of fruit, yield, wool, milk, service, or dwelling. This affects the default scope.
2
Check for the word 'abad'
For fruit, if 'abad' (forever) is added, it includes future; otherwise only existing. For yield, 'abad' is irrelevant as it always includes future. For wool and milk, even 'abad' does not include future.
3
Apply the default rule for each type
'Ghallah' automatically covers both present and future yields. 'Thamar' is limited to existing fruit without 'abad'. Wool and milk are limited to what exists at death regardless of wording.
4
Apply the three-category framework
The passage summarizes three categories: (1) bequests that always include future (service, dwelling, yield), (2) bequests that never include future (milk in udder, wool on back, offspring in womb), (3) bequests that include future only if 'abad' is mentioned (fruit).

Source Text

ولو مات إلخ : أي لو مات الموصى له قبل موت الموصي بطلت الوصية؛ لأنها تمليك مضاف إلى ما بعد الموت، وفي الحال ملك الموصي ثابت فيه، ولا يتصور تملك الموح له بعد ،موته فبطلت تكملة البحر الرائق: ٣٦٠/٩] هذه الثمرة: أي إذا أوصى بثمرة بستانه، ثم مات وفيه ثمرة، كان للموصى هذه الثمرة وحدها؛ لأن الثمرة اسم لموجود عرفا، فلا يتناول المعدوم إلا بدلالة زائدة مثل التنصيص على الأبد ؛ إذ لا يتأبد إلا بتناول المعدوم، وإليه أشار بقوله: "فإن "زاد أي إن زاد الموصي في وصيته بثمرة بستانه قوله: "أبدا" بأن قال: "له ثمرة بستاني أبدا" كان للموصى له هذه الثمرة فيما يستقبل من ثمرته ما عاش رمز الحقائق: ٤٩٠/٢] (بزيادة) كغلة بستانه : أي كما إذا أوصى بغلة بستانه فله أي للموصى له الغلة القائمة فيه وغلته فيما يستقبل؛ لأن الغلة تنتظم الموجود، وما يكون بعرض الوجود مرة أخرى عرفا، بخلاف الثمرة إذا أطلقت لا تتناول إلا الموجود، فالحاصل أنه إذا أوصى بالغلة استحقه دائما، وبالثمرة لا يستحق إلا القائم إلا إذا زاد "أبدا"، والفرق ما ذكرنا، وإنما قيد بقوله: وفيه مرة ؛ لأنه إذا لم يكن فيه ثمرة، والمسألة بحالها، فهي كمسألة الغلة في تناولها الثمرة المعدومة ما عاش الموصى له رمز الحقائق: ٤٩٠/٢] وبصوف غنمه إلخ : أي إذا أوصى بهذه الأشياء كان له الموجود عند موته، ولا يستحق ما سيحدث بعد موته سواء قال: "أبدا" أو لم يقل؛ لأنه إيجاب عند الموت، فيعتبر وجود هذه الأشياء عنده، لكن جازت الوصية في الغلة المعدومة والثمرة المعدومة على ما بينا؛ لأنها تستحق بغير الوصية من العقود كالمزارعة والمعاملة، فلأن تستحق بالوصية أولى؛ لأنها أوسع بابا من غيرها والحاصل أن مسائل هذا الباب على ثلاثة أوجه: كما في "الزيلعي"، منها ما يقع على الموجود والمعدوم ذكر الأبد أو لم يذكر ، كالوصية بالخدمة والسكنى والغلة والثمرة، ولم تكن موجودة عند موته ومنها ما يقع على الموجود دون المعدوم ذكر الأبد أو لم يذكر، كالوصية باللبن في الضرع، والصوف على الظهر، والولد في البطن، ومنها: ما يقع على الموجود والمعدوم إن ذكر الأبد، وإلا فعلى الموجود فقط، كالوصية بثمرة وفيه ثمرة تكملة البحر الرائق: ٣٦١/٩] (فتح)
Book of Wills. Bequest of service, dwelling, and fruit. If he dies during the life of the testator, it is void. And with the fruit of his garden, he dies, and there is fruit in it, he has this (current fruit). And the situation is that in the garden, for the legatee, i.e., even if he bequeaths the fruit. If he adds 'forever', he has this and what will come in the future, like the yield of his garden. And with the wool of his sheep and their milk, he has what exists at his death, whether he said 'forever' or not. The existing (fruit) alone for the legatee. The testator... and its offspring. 'If he dies etc.' i.e., if the legatee dies before the testator's death, the bequest is void because it is a transfer of ownership attached to after death, and currently the testator's ownership is established in it, and ownership for the legatee after his death is inconceivable, so it becomes void. (Completion of al-Bahr al-Raiq 9:360). 'This fruit' i.e., if he bequeaths the fruit of his garden, then he dies and there is fruit in it, the legatee gets this fruit alone, because 'fruit' is a name for what exists customarily, so it does not include what is non-existent except with an additional indication such as specifying 'forever', since it is only perpetual by including what is non-existent. This is indicated by his saying: 'If he adds' i.e., if the testator adds in his bequest of the fruit of his garden the word 'forever' by saying 'he has the fruit of my garden forever', the legatee gets this fruit and what will come of its fruit as long as he lives. (Ramz al-Haqaiq 2:490). 'With an increase' like the yield of his garden i.e., just as if he bequeaths the yield of his garden, the legatee gets the yield existing in it and its future yield, because 'yield' comprises what exists and what is likely to exist repeatedly customarily, unlike 'fruit' when unrestricted does not include except what exists. So the conclusion is that if he bequeaths the yield, he gets it perpetually, and with fruit he only gets the existing unless he adds 'forever'. And the difference is what we mentioned. He restricted it with 'and there is fruit in it' because if there is no fruit, and the case is as it is, it is like the case of yield in including the non-existent fruit as long as the legatee lives. (Ramz al-Haqaiq 2:490). 'And with the wool of his sheep etc.' i.e., if he bequeaths these things, he gets what exists at his death, and he does not get what will arise after his death, whether he said 'forever' or not, because it is an obligation at death, so the existence of these things at the time is considered. However, the bequest of non-existent yield and non-existent fruit is valid as we explained, because it is acquired through other contracts like sharecropping and shareholding, so it is more appropriate to be acquired through bequest because it is broader in scope than others. The summary is that the issues of this chapter are of three types, as in al-Zayla'i: one type applies to both existing and non-existent whether 'forever' is mentioned or not, like bequest of service, dwelling, yield, and fruit, even if they did not exist at the time of death; another type applies to existing only, not non-existent, whether 'forever' is mentioned or not, like bequest of milk in the udder, wool on the back, and offspring in the womb; and a third type applies to both existing and non-existent if 'forever' is mentioned, otherwise only to existing, like bequest of fruit when there is fruit (at death). (Completion of al-Bahr al-Raiq 9:361) (Fath).
Source pages p. 500

Commentary
This passage from the commentary on Kanz al-Daqa'iq explains the rulings regarding bequests of items that can generate future yields, such as fruit, wool, milk, and service. The key distinction is between 'thamar' (fruit) and 'ghallah' (yield). Customarily, 'fruit' only refers to existing fruit unless the testator explicitly adds the word 'abad' (forever) to include future fruit. In contrast, 'yield' inherently includes both present and future produce. Similarly, bequests of wool and milk only cover what exists at the testator's death, regardless of mentioning 'forever', because these are considered property attached to the animal (like a part of it) and cannot include future growth. The passage then summarizes three categories: (1) bequests that always include future items (like service and dwelling), (2) those that only include present (like milk and wool), and (3) those that include future only if 'forever' is mentioned (like fruit). This is based on customary usage and the nature of the bequest. The commentary also clarifies that if the legatee dies before the testator, the bequest becomes void because it is a contingent transfer after death.

Key Terms
ثمرة (thamar): Fruit; customarily only refers to existing produce unless specified otherwise.
غلة (ghallah): Yield or produce; includes both existing and future yields by custom.
أبد (abad): Forever; when added to a bequest, extends it to include future items.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the ruling if someone bequeaths 'the fruit of my garden' without adding 'forever', and at the time of death there is fruit on the trees?
A) The legatee gets only the existing fruit.
B) The legatee gets the existing fruit and all future fruit.
C) The bequest is void because fruit is not specified.
D) The legatee gets nothing because fruit is not owned yet.

Key Takeaway
Bequests are interpreted based on custom; 'thamar' is limited to existing unless 'abad' is used, but 'ghallah' always includes future; wool and milk never include future growth.

The Dhimmi's Will to Build a Church: Intra-Hanafi Dispute
Explains the validity of a dhimmi's will for church building with intra-Hanafi dispute.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the positions of Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn on a dhimmi's will to build a church, explain their proofs, and classify this will within the three categories of dhimmi wills.

Core Idea
A dhimmi's bequest to build a church is valid according to Abu Hanifa but invalid according to his two disciples.

The will of a dhimmi to convert his house into a place of worship raises a fascinating intra-Hanafi dispute: is it a valid act of devotion in the dhimmi's belief, or is it a sin under Islamic law? This lesson unpacks the reasoning of Abu Hanifa and his two chief disciples, Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani, and shows how their disagreement fits into a larger three-fold classification of dhimmi wills.

Guided Path
1
Identify the legal act and the core dispute
The act is a dhimmi's bequest that his house be turned into a church or synagogue. Determine whether this bequest is valid (executed from one-third of the estate) or invalid.
The act is disputed: Abu Hanifa says valid; Sahibayn say invalid.
2
State Abu Hanifa's position and his proof
Abu Hanifa rules the bequest valid because building a church is a good deed (qurbah) in the dhimmi's religion, and Muslims are commanded to leave dhimmis to their beliefs. This is a rational argument (dalil aqli).
He also notes that if the bequest is for specified people, it becomes a transfer of ownership, which is always valid from one-third.
3
State the Sahibayn's position and their proof
Abu Yusuf and Muhammad rule the bequest invalid because building a church is a sin (ma'siyah) in Islamic law. Even if it is good in the dhimmi's belief, a bequest of sin is void.
They argue that executing a sin is not permitted, regardless of the testator's intention.
4
Follow the objection to Abu Hanifa and his response
An objection: If a mosque is inviolable and cannot be sold, why isn't a church likewise? Abu Hanifa's response: A mosque is exclusively for Allah, but a church remains for human uses (dwelling, storing wealth), so ownership is not fully removed; thus, it can be inherited and bequeathed.
This addresses the analogy to waqf.
5
Categorize this will within the three-fold classification
The passage presents three categories of dhimmi wills: (1) valid by consensus (good in both religions), (2) invalid by consensus (sin in both), and (3) disputed (this case: good in dhimmi belief, sin in Islam). Place the current case in the third category.
This helps see the broader framework of Hanafi fiqh on dhimmi wills.

Source Text

باب وصية الذمي: لما فرغ من وصية المسلمين شرع في وصية أهل الكتاب وترجم بالذمي؛ لأنه ملحق بالمسلمين في المعاملات تكملة البحر الرائق: ٣٦٤/٩] فهي ميراث بالاتفاق أما عند أبي حنيفة؛ فإنه بمنزلة الوقف عنده، والوقف لا يلزم فيورث، فكذا هذا، وأما عندهما؛ فلأن هذا معصية، فلا تصح، وإن كان قربة في معتقدهم. رمز الحقائق: ٤٩١/٢] بقي إشكال على قول أبي حنيفة، وهو أن هذا عندهم كالمسجد عندنا والمسلم ليس له أن يبيع المسجد، فوجب أن يكون الذمي كذلك؛ لأنهم عنده يتركون وما يعتقدون، وجوابه: أن المسجد محرز عن حقوق العباد، فصار خالصا الله، ولا كذلك البيع في حقهم، فإنها لمنافع الناس؛ لأنهم يسكنون فيها، ويدفنون فيها ،أموالهم، فلم تصر محرزة عن حقوقهم، فكان ملكه فيها تاما، وفي هذه الصورة يورث المسجد أيضا على ما يجيء بيانه تكملة البحر الرائق: ٤٦٤/٩]

الثلث أي إذا أوصى أن يبنى داره بيعة أو كنيسة لقوم معينين فهو جائز من الثلث؛ لأن الوصية فيها التمليك، فأمكن تصحيحها على اعتبار المعنيين تكملة البحر الرائق: ٣٦٥/٩] صحت: أي صحت وصيته، وهذا عند أبي حنيفة، وقالا: هي باطلة؛ لكونها معصية رمز الحقائق: ٤٩١/٢] وإن كان في معتقدهم ،قربة والوصية بالمعصية باطلة؛ لأن تنفيذها تقرير للمعصية، ولأبي حنيفة: أن هذه قربة في معتقدهم، ونحن أمرنا أن نتركهم وما يدينون، فيجوز بناء على معتقدهم، ألا ترى أنه لو أوصى بما هو قربة حقيقة، وهو معصية في معتقدهم لا تجوز الوصية اعتبارا لاعتقادهم، فكذا عكسه. ثم الفرق لأبي حنيفة بين بنائها وبين الوصية أن البناء ليس بسبب لزوال الملك بخلاف الوصية؛ فإنها وضعت لإزالة الملك، هذا إذا أوصى ببنائها في القرى، وأما في الأمصار فلا يجوز بالاتفاق؛ لأنهم لا يمكنون البيعة في الأمصار وعلى هذا الخلاف إذا أوصى بأن تذبح خنازيره، ويطعم المشركون من غير تعيين؛ لما ذكرنا، وإن كان لقوم معينين جاز بالاتفاق على أنه تمليك. والحاصل أن وصايا الذمي ثلاثة أقسام: أحدها: جائز بالاتفاق، كما إذا أوصى بما هو قربة عندنا وعندهم، مثل: أن بأن يسرج في بيت المقدس، أو بأن يغزى الترك، وهو من الروم، سواء كان لقوم معينين أو لم يكن، الثاني: باطل بالاتفاق كما إذا أوصى بما ليس بقربة عندنا وعندهم، مثل أن للمغنيات والنائحات أو أوصى بما . قربة عندنا، وليس بقربة عندهم، مثل أن يوصي بالحج أو ببناء مسجد للمسلمين، أو بأن تسرج مساجدهم؛ لأنه معصية عندهم إلا أن  
يكون لقوم بأعيانهم، فيصح باعتبار التمليك، الثالث: مختلف فيه وهو المذكور الآن. رمز الحقائق: ٤٩١/٢] (تكملة)
Chapter on the Will of the Dhimmi. A dhimmi who turns his house into a church or synagogue during his health, then dies, it is inheritance. And if he bequeaths that, he is the place of worship of Christians, the place of worship of Jews, or a fire temple. For named people, it is from the third; and with his house a church for unnamed people, it is valid. i.e., specified. i.e., if he bequeaths that a church be built. Chapter on the Will of the Dhimmi: When he finished from the will of Muslims, he began on the will of the People of the Book and titled with 'dhimmi' because he is attached to Muslims in transactions. (Completion of al-Bahr al-Raiq 9:364) So it is inheritance by agreement. As for Abu Hanifa, it is like a waqf in his view, and waqf is not binding, so it is inherited, thus this. As for the two (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad), because this is a sin, it is not valid, even if it is a good deed in their belief. (Ramz al-Haqaiq 2:491) There remains an objection to Abu Hanifa's statement: this is like a mosque for us, and a Muslim cannot sell a mosque, so the dhimmi should be the same because they are left to their beliefs. The answer: the mosque is protected from the rights of people, so it becomes purely for Allah, but not so the church in their case, because it is for the benefits of people; they dwell in it, bury their wealth in it, so it is not protected from their rights, so his ownership is complete. And in this case, the mosque is also inherited as will be explained. (Completion of al-Bahr al-Raiq 9:464) So it is from the third. i.e., if he bequeaths to build his house as a church for specified people, it is permissible from the third because the bequest involves transfer of ownership, so it can be corrected based on both meanings. (Completion of al-Bahr al-Raiq 9:365) 'Valid' i.e., his bequest is valid, and this is according to Abu Hanifa, but they (the two) said it is void because it is a sin. (Ramz al-Haqaiq 2:491) Even if it is a good deed in their belief, a bequest of sin is void because its execution affirms the sin. For Abu Hanifa: this is a good deed in their belief, and we are commanded to leave them and their religion, so it is permissible based on their belief. Do you not see that if he bequeaths what is truly a good deed, which is a sin in their belief, the bequest is not valid considering their belief, and so is its opposite. Then the distinction for Abu Hanifa between building and bequest: building is not a cause for removal of ownership, unlike the bequest which is established to remove ownership. This if he bequeaths its building in villages, but in cities it is not permissible by agreement because they are not allowed to have churches in cities. And on this difference, if he bequeaths that his pigs be slaughtered and the polytheists be fed without specification; as we mentioned. And if it is for specified people, it is permissible by agreement as a transfer of ownership. The summary: the wills of a dhimmi are of three types: one: permissible by agreement, as when he bequeaths what is a good deed for us and them, such as to light lamps in Jerusalem, or to fight the Turks while he is from the Romans, whether for specified people or not. Second: void by agreement, as when he bequeaths what is not a good deed for us or them, such as for female singers and wailers, or bequeaths... a good deed for us but not for them, such as bequeathing Hajj or building a mosque for Muslims, or lighting their mosques; because it is a sin in their belief unless it is for specified individuals, then it is valid as a transfer of ownership. Third: disputed, which is the one mentioned now. (Ramz al-Haqaiq 2:491) (Completion).
Source pages p. 500

Commentary
This passage from the commentary on Kanz al-Daqa'iq discusses the rulings concerning a dhimmi's will. It focuses on the case where a dhimmi bequeaths that his house be converted into a church or synagogue. The chapter begins by noting that if a dhimmi physically converts his house during his lifetime, it is considered inheritance (i.e., the act is not binding and the house remains inheritable). However, if he makes a will to that effect, there is an intra-Hanafi dispute: Abu Hanifa validates the will on the grounds that building a church is a good deed in the dhimmi's religious belief, and we are commanded to leave them to their religion. The two disciples (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) consider it a sin and invalid, even if it is a good deed in their belief, because it is sinful in Islamic law. The commentary then addresses an objection to Abu Hanifa's view: if a mosque is inviolable, why isn't a church likewise? The answer is that a mosque is exclusively for Allah, whereas a church is used for human purposes like dwelling and storing wealth, so ownership is not fully removed. The passage further explains that if the dhimmi designates specific people to receive the church, the bequest is valid from one-third of his estate, as it becomes a transfer of ownership. The chapter concludes with a three-fold categorization of a dhimmi's wills: (1) valid by consensus (e.g., bequests that are good deeds in both Islam and their religion), (2) invalid by consensus (e.g., bequests that are sinful in both), and (3) disputed (the case of building a church).

Key Terms
ذمي (dhimmi): A non-Muslim subject living under Muslim rule with a covenant of protection.
بيعة (bi'ah): Church or place of worship for Christians.
قربة (qurbah): A good deed that brings one closer to God.
معصية (ma'siyah): Sin; an act that is forbidden or opposed to Islamic law.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, which of the following is true about a dhimmi's will to build a church?
A) It is valid by consensus of the Hanafi school.
B) It is invalid by consensus because building a church is a sin.
C) Abu Hanifa validates it; the Sahibayn invalidate it.
D) It is valid only if the church is built in a city.

Key Takeaway
A dhimmi's bequest to build a church is valid according to Abu Hanifa but invalid according to his two disciples, with the practical ruling depending on whether the bequest is for specified people and the location (village vs. city).

Executor's Division and Legatee's Right to Reclaim Lost Share
Ruling on executor's division and legatee's recourse when share is lost

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the ruling when an executor divides the estate and the legatee's share is lost, and explain the Hanafi reasoning based on the analogy to sale.

Core Idea
The legatee's share lost after executor's division is not forfeited; he reclaims one-third of what remains.

Imagine you are appointed as an executor of a will. You divide the estate among the heirs and set aside the legatee's share, but that share is subsequently lost. Can the legatee still claim from the remaining estate? The Hanafi school provides a clear ruling based on the nature of division and the executor's authority. This lesson unpacks the legal reasoning behind that ruling.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
What exactly is being ruled upon? The executor's division of the estate with the heirs, including the legatee's share. The ruling is that the division is valid in itself, but if the legatee's share is lost, the legatee has recourse.
The passage says 'رجع بثلث ما بقي' – he returns to a third of what remains.
2
Locate the proof (dalil)
The proof is qiyas (analogy) to a sale. The text states: 'القسمة في معنى البيع' – division is in the meaning of sale. The executor has authority to sell for minors and preserve for adults, so division is permissible by analogy.
The analogy is jaliy (clear) because both involve transfer of ownership.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
How does the analogy prove the ruling? Just as a sale by the executor does not require the minor's consent, division similarly does not require the legatee's immediate acceptance. However, the legatee retains ownership rights until he accepts.
This is why the division is not final with respect to the legatee.
4
Identify the exception
An exception is immovable property: 'إلا العقار فإنه محفوظ بنفسه' – except immovable property, which is self-preserved, so the executor cannot sell it. This is because the illa (preservation) does not apply.
This shows the scope of the analogy.
5
Apply the ruling to the scenario
If the executor divides and the legatee's share is lost, the legatee can take a third of what remains of the estate (not of the original share). If the division was ordered by a qadi, it is binding and no recourse.
The reversal case (executor representing legatee) is invalid because the executor is not a complete representative.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
أحكام الوصي ولو عكس لا، فلو قاسم الورثة، وأخذ نصيب الموصى له، فضاع رجع بثلث ما ذلك النصيب الموصى له بقي، وإن أوصى الميت بحجة، فقاسم الورثة، فهلك ما في يده، أو دفع إلى من يحج عنه، فضاع في يده حج عن الميت بثلث ما بقي، وصح قسمة القاضي عليه غير ذلك ما في يد الوصي ليس له أن يشارك الموصى له رمز الحقائق: ٤٩٣/٢] ولا فرق في ذلك بين أن يكون الورثة كبارا أو صغارا؛ لأن له ولاية البيع في مال الصغار، والقسمة في معنى البيع وله ولاية الحفظ في مال الكبار، فجاز له بيعه للحفظ إلا العقار فإنه محفوظ بنفسه، فلا يجوز له بيعه، وهذا في معنى البيع، فلا يضمن. (عيني بزيادة تصرف) ولو عكس :لا على صيغة المجهول أي ولو عكس الحكم المذكور لا يصح، وفي بعض النسخ: "وعكسه لا"، وهو ما إذا قاسم الوصي الورثة نائبا عن الموصى له فلا يجوز؛ لأن الوصي ليس بخليفة عن الميت من كل وجه، فلا يكون خصما عنه عند غيبته، حتى لو هلك ما أفرز له عند الوصي، كان له ثلث ما بقي؛ لأن القسمة لم تنفذ أن الوصي لا يضمن؛ لأنه أمين فيه وله ولاية الحفظ رمز الحقائق: ٤٩٣/٢] فلو قاسم إلخ : أي لو قاسم الوصي الورثة، وأخذ نصيب الموصى له فضاع ذلك في يده، رجع الموصى له بثلث ما بقي؛ لما بينا أن الموصى له شريك الورثة، فيرجع الموصى له على ما في يد الورثة إن كان باقيا، فيأخذ بثلثه؛ لعدم صحة القسمة في حقه، وإذا هلك في أيديهم فله أن يضمنهم قدر ثلث ما قبضوا، وإن شاء ضمن الوصي القدر؛ لأنه متعد فيه بالدفع إليهم، والورثة بالقبض فيضمن أيهما شاء تكملة البحر الرائق: ٣٨٥/٩] بثلث ما بقي من التركة لو قائما بيد الورثة، ولو قسم بأمر القاضي جاز، ولا رجوع.
Rulings of the executor: If reversed, no. So if he divided with the heirs and took the legatee's share and it was lost, he (the legatee) returns to a third of what remains of that share. And if the deceased made a bequest for Hajj and he divided with the heirs and what was in his hand perished, or he paid someone to perform Hajj on his behalf and it perished in his hand, Hajj is performed on behalf of the deceased from a third of what remains. And the division of the qadi is valid. Otherwise, what is in the executor's hand: he does not have the right to participate with the legatee. [Ramz al-Haqaiq 2/493] And there is no difference in that between the heirs being adults or minors, because he has authority to sell from the property of minors, and division is in the meaning of sale, and he has authority of preservation over the property of adults, so it is permissible for him to sell for preservation, except immovable property, which is self-preserved, so it is not permissible for him to sell. And this is in the meaning of sale, so he does not guarantee. (Ayni with additional modification) And its reverse is no, on the passive form, meaning if the mentioned ruling is reversed it is not valid. In some copies: 'And its reverse is no.' That is when the executor divides with the heirs representing the legatee, then it is not permissible because the executor is not a deputy of the deceased in every respect, so he is not a litigant on his behalf in his absence. Even if what was separated for him perished with the executor, he has a third of what remains because the division is not executed. The executor does not guarantee because he is a trustee over it and has authority of preservation. [Ramz al-Haqaiq 2/493] So if he divided, etc.: That is, if the executor divided with the heirs and took the legatee's share and it perished in his hand, the legatee returns to a third of what remains, because as we explained, the legatee is a partner with the heirs. So the legatee resorts to what is in the hands of the heirs if it remains, and takes its third, because the division is not valid with respect to him. And if it perished in their hands, he can hold them liable for the amount of a third of what they took, and if he wishes he can hold the executor liable for the amount because he transgressed by paying to them, and the heirs by taking, so he holds liable whichever he wishes. [Bahr al-Ra'iq 9/385] By a third of what remains of the estate if it is still in the hands of the heirs. And if he divided by order of the qadi, it is valid and there is no recourse.
Source pages p. 506

Commentary
This passage from Kitab al-Wasaya presents a ruling from Ahkam al-Wasi (rulings of the executor). The base matn states: 'ولو عكس لا' meaning if the executor acts in reverse (i.e., representing the legatee against the heirs), the division is invalid. Then it clarifies the scenario: if the executor divides the estate with the heirs and takes the legatee's share, and that share is subsequently lost, the legatee can take a third of what remains of the estate. The commentary expands on this, explaining that the executor has authority over minors' property and that division is analogous to sale, which is why he can do it. However, immovable property is excluded because it is self-preserving. The reversal case (executor representing legatee) is invalid because the executor is not a complete representative of the deceased in all matters, so he cannot be a litigant for the legatee. The legatee, being a partner with the heirs, can reclaim from the remaining estate. If the qadi ordered the division, it is valid and the legatee cannot reclaim. The reasoning is based on qiyas (analogy to sale) and the executor's authority of preservation.

Key Terms
الوصي (al-wasi): The executor appointed to carry out the deceased's will and manage the estate.
القسمة (al-qismah): Division of the estate among heirs and legatees.
الموصى له (al-musa lahu): The legatee, the person in whose favor a bequest is made.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
If an executor divides the estate, takes the legatee's share, and that share is lost, what recourse does the legatee have?
A) The legatee loses the bequest entirely.
B) The legatee can take a third of what remains of the estate.
C) The legatee can only sue the executor for negligence.
D) The legatee must accept the loss if the heirs are minors.

Key Takeaway
The executor's division of an estate does not extinguish the legatee's right; if the legatee's share is lost, he can reclaim one-third of what remains, based on the analogy that division is like a sale that does not complete ownership without acceptance.

Validity of Qadi's Division for Absent Legatee
Ruling on qadi's division for absent legatee with proof and consequence

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on a qadi's division of an estate for an absent legatee, explain the legal basis for its validity, and identify the consequences if the share is lost.

Core Idea
A qadi's division for an absent legatee is valid and binding; loss of the share gives no recourse.

In this passage from a classical Hanafi text, we examine the ruling concerning a qadi (judge) dividing the estate of a deceased when the legatee is absent. The text establishes that such a division is valid, and importantly, if the legatee's share perishes in the qadi's custody, the legatee cannot reclaim from the heirs or the qadi. Understanding this requires appreciating the Hanafi principle that a bequest to an absent person is valid even before acceptance, and the qadi acts as a guardian for the incapable.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Act and Ruling
Read the passage and determine what legal act is being ruled upon. The act is the qadi's division of the estate (qismat al-qadi) on behalf of an absent legatee. The ruling is that this division is valid (sahih) and binding.
The text begins with 'قسمة القاضي' and proceeds to affirm its validity.
2
Locate the Dalil (Legal Basis)
Find the reason given for the validity. The text states 'لأن الوصية للغائب صحيحة' (because a bequest to an absent person is valid) and adds that it is valid even before acceptance. This principle is the proof that the qadi's action is grounded in a valid right.
The dalil is not a specific verse or hadith but a recognized legal maxim in the Hanafi school.
3
Understand the Qadi's Role
The passage explains that the qadi is a supervisor over the right of the incapable (ناظر في حق العاجز). The legatee is absent, hence unable to act. Separating the share and taking possession is part of that supervision.
This establishes the qadi's authority to act on behalf of the absent legatee.
4
Derive the Consequence
If the share is lost after being taken by the qadi or his trustee, the legatee has no recourse against the heirs or the qadi ('لم يكن له على الورثة سبيل ولا على القاضي'). The division is final.
This consequence follows from the validity of the division; once validly separated, risk passes to the legatee.
5
Distinguish from Other Scenarios
Consider the difference from an executor's division, which might be revocable. The qadi's authority as a judge makes his division binding even on absent persons, unlike a private executor.
This is implied by the text's emphasis on the qadi's role as guardian.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قسمة القاضي إلخ: يعني صح قسمة القاضي التركة مع الورثة نائبا عن الموصى له، وصح أخذ حظ وصح الموصى له إن غاب الموصى له؛ لأن الوصية للغائب صحيحة وإن كان قبل القبول ولهذا لو مات الموصى له قبل القبول تصير الوصية ميراثا لورثته والقاضي ناظر في حق العاجز، وإفراز نصيب الغائب وقبضه من النظر، حتى لو حضر الغائب، وقد هلك المقبوض في يد القاضي أو أمينه لم يكن له على الورثة سبيل، ولا على القاضي، -
Division of the qadi, etc.: That is, the division of the estate by the qadi with the heirs is valid, representing the legatee, and taking the share is valid, and the legatee is valid even if absent, because a bequest to an absent person is valid even before acceptance. For this reason, if the legatee dies before acceptance, the bequest becomes inheritance for his heirs. The qadi is a supervisor over the right of the incapable, and separating the share of the absent one and taking possession of it is part of supervision. Even if the absent one appears and the possession perished in the hand of the qadi or his trustee, he has no recourse against the heirs nor against the qadi.
Source pages p. 506

Commentary
This passage deals with the validity of a qadi (judge) dividing the estate of a deceased when the legatee is absent. The ruling is that the qadi can validly divide the estate with the heirs on behalf of the absent legatee, and the legatee's share is validly set aside. This is because a bequest to an absent person is valid (even before the legatee accepts it), as evidenced by the fact that if the legatee dies before acceptance, the bequest becomes part of his inheritance. The qadi has authority over the interests of those unable to act for themselves (like an absent person). Therefore, if the qadi takes possession of the legatee's share and it is later lost while in the qadi's or his agent's custody, the legatee cannot claim compensation from the heirs or the qadi. The rationale is that the qadi's division is valid and final, unlike the executor's division which may be contested.

Key Terms
القاضي (al-qadi): The judge who has authority over the estate in absence of the legatee.
الوصية للغائب (al-wasiyyah lil-gha'ib): A bequest to an absent person is valid even before acceptance.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, if an absent legatee's share is lost after the qadi takes possession, what recourse does the legatee have?
A) He can reclaim from the heirs.
B) He can sue the qadi.
C) He has no recourse against the heirs or the qadi.
D) He can void the bequest.

Key Takeaway
A qadi's division of an estate for an absent legatee is final and binding; loss of the share does not create liability for the heirs or the qadi.

The Hanafi Priority of the Father's Executor over the Grandfather
Dispute between Hanafi and Shafi'i on priority of executor over grandfather

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi position on the priority of the father's executor over the grandfather and evaluate the Shafi'i counter-argument.

Core Idea
The father's executor appointed by him takes precedence over the grandfather because the father's authority transfers by explicit delegation.

In this lesson, we examine a key dispute between the Hanafi and Shafi'i schools regarding who should manage the property of a minor when the father has appointed an executor. The Hanafi school holds that the executor (waṣī) appointed by the father is more entitled than the paternal grandfather (jadd). The Shafi'i school argues that the grandfather, as the closest relative, takes precedence. We will explore the reasoning and practical implication of this difference.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi position
The matn states that the father's executor is more entitled to the child's property than the grandfather.
This is the basic ruling from the text.
2
Identify the opposing view
Imam al-Shafi'i argues that the grandfather is more entitled because the Law has established him in the father's place in his absence.
Shafi'i relies on the idea of legal substitution.
3
Analyze the Hanafi proof
The Hanafi proof is that the father's authority transfers to the executor by appointment, so the executor effectively represents the father. The father's choice, knowing the grandfather, indicates the executor is more beneficial.
The proof is based on the father's explicit delegation and its implications.
4
Determine the practical consequence
If the father appointed an executor, the executor manages the property; otherwise, the grandfather does.
This is the thamarah al-khilaf (practical difference).

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ووصي الأب أحق بمال الطفل من الجد، فإن لم يوص الأب، فالجد كالأب.
ووصي الأب أحق إلخ وقال الشافعي له الجدّ أحق؛ لأن الشرع أقامه مقام الأب عند عدمه حتى أحرز ميراثه فيتقدم على وصيه ولنا أن ولاية الأب تنتقل إليه بالإيصاء، فكانت ولايته قائمة معنى، فيقدم عليه كالأب نفسه؛ لأن اختياره مع علمه بالجد يدل على أن تصرفه أنظر لأولاده من تصرف الجد. رمز الحقائق: ٤٩٥/٢] فالجد كالأب: يعني إن لم يوص الأب فالجد كالأب؛ لأنه أقرب الناس إليه، حتى ملك الإنكاح دون الوصي. تكملة البحر الرائق: ٣٨٩/٩]
And the father's executor is more entitled to the child's property than the grandfather. If the father did not appoint an executor, then the grandfather is like the father. And the father's executor is more entitled, etc. Al-Shafi'i said: the grandfather is more entitled because the Law has established him in place of the father in his absence, so he inherits from him, so he takes precedence over his executor. Our proof: the father's authority transfers to the executor through appointment, so his authority is effectively existing, so he takes precedence like the father himself, because his choice, knowing the grandfather, indicates that his action is more considerate for his children than the grandfather's action. The grandfather is like the father: meaning if the father did not appoint an executor, then the grandfather is like the father, for he is the closest relative, so he has the right of marriage contract, unlike the executor.
Source pages p. 509

Commentary
This passage is an inter-madhhab dispute between Hanafi and Shafi'i. The matn states that the father's executor is more entitled to manage the child's property than the grandfather. Al-Shafi'i argues that the grandfather, being the closest relative by law, takes precedence. The Hanafi response is that the father's authority transfers to the executor by appointment, so the executor effectively represents the father. The father's choice of executor over the grandfather implies that the executor's management is more beneficial. If the father did not appoint an executor, then the grandfather takes the father's place, as he is the natural guardian.

Key Terms
الجد (al-jadd): The paternal grandfather of the minor.
الوصي (al-waṣī): The executor appointed by the father.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, who is more entitled to manage the minor's property if the father appointed an executor?
A) The grandfather.
B) The executor appointed by the father.
C) The mother.
D) The judge.

Key Takeaway
The father's appointed executor takes precedence over the grandfather in managing the minor's property because the father's authority transfers by explicit delegation.

Testimony of Two Groups in Bequests: The Primary Ruling
Primary ruling on mutual testimony in bequests with reasoning.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on the acceptance of mutual testimony in bequest claims and explain Muhammad al-Shaybani's reasoning based on the capacity of the dhimmah.

Core Idea
Debt in the dhimmah is separate — mutual testimony is accepted because no partnership arises from distinct causes.

This lesson examines the primary ruling in the passage: the testimony of two groups, each claiming a bequest of 1000, is accepted when they testify for each other. The key legal point is that the debt is obligated in the dhimmah (legal personality), which can bear multiple rights, so no partnership is created. This is the view of Muhammad al-Shaybani.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is two groups testifying for each other regarding separate bequests. The ruling is that the testimony is accepted (sahih).
2
Locate the evidence
The evidence is the principle that debt is in the dhimmah, which is capable of multiple obligations. This is supported by qiyas: if a stranger pays the debt of one, the other has no share.
The text uses talil (rational reasoning) to establish the ruling.
3
Understand the condition
The testimony is accepted only if the debts arise from separate causes. If a single cause, partnership would exist and testimony would be rejected.
The condition is that the debts are not from a single obligation.
4
Note the exception
When the items bequeathed are different (e.g., slave vs. female slave), testimony is accepted by consensus because no partnership is created.
This shows the decisive factor is whether partnership is established.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
كتاب الوصايا
أحكام الشهادة
تقبل، وإن كانت شهادة كل فريق بوصية ألف، لا. للآخر
تقبل: أي تقبل شهادة الفريقين؛ لأن الدين يجب في الذمة، وهي قابلة لحقوق شتى، فلا شركة فيه إذا لم يجب بسبب واحد، ولهذا لو تبرع أجنبي بقضاء دين أحدهما، لم يكن للآخر حق المشاركة، وهذا عند محمد، خلافا لأبي يوسف، ويروى أن أبا حنيفة مع محمد ويروى مع أبي يوسف، وعن أبي يوسف مثل قول محمد، وعن الحسن عن أبي حنيفة أنهم إذا جاءوا معا، وشهدوا فالشهادة باطلة. (فتح عيني) لا: أي لا تقبل الشهادة؛ لأن فيه إثبات الشركة وفيه التهمة، وكذلك إذا شهد الأولان أن الميت أوصى لهذين الرجلين بعبده، وشهد المشهود لهما أنه أوصى للأولين بثلث ماله فهي باطلة؛ لأن الشهادة في هذه الصور مثبتة للشركة، كما في "الهداية"، بخلاف ما إذا شهدا أنه أوصى لهذين الرجلين بجاريته، وشهد المشهود لهما أنه أوصى للشاهدين بعبده، حيث تجوز الشهادة بالاتفاق؛ لعدم الشركة فلا تهمة وقال أبو يوسف: لا تقبل في الدين أيضا؛ لأن الدين بالموت يتعلق بالتركة؛ إذ الذمة خربت بالموت ولهذا لو استوفى أحدهما حقه من التركة يشاركه الآخر فيه، فكانت الشهادة مثبتة حق الشركة فتحققت التهمة بخلاف حال حياة المديون حيث تجوز شهادة الغرماء بعضهم لبعض؛ لأنه في الذمة؛ لبقائها لا في المال، فلا يتحقق الشركة، كذا في "الهداية" بقليل زيادة للإيضاح. (فتح)
Book of Wills. Rulings of Testimony. [It is] accepted, even if the testimony of each group is for a bequest of a thousand, not for the other. [It is] accepted: meaning the testimony of both groups is accepted because the debt is obligated in the dhimmah (legal personality), and it is receptive to various rights, so there is no partnership in it when it is not obligated due to one cause. For this reason, if a stranger voluntarily pays the debt of one of them, the other has no right of participation. This is according to Muhammad, contrary to Abu Yusuf. It is narrated that Abu Hanifa is with Muhammad, and it is narrated that he is with Abu Yusuf. And from Abu Yusuf a statement like Muhammad's. And from al-Hasan from Abu Hanifa: if they come together and testify, the testimony is void. (Fath 'Ayni) 'No': meaning the testimony is not accepted because it involves establishing partnership and there is suspicion (tuhma). Similarly, if the first two testify that the deceased bequeathed his slave to these two men, and the two beneficiaries testify that he bequeathed one-third of his wealth to the first two, it is void because the testimony in these cases establishes partnership, as in al-Hidayah. Contrary to the case where they testify that he bequeathed his female slave to these two men, and the beneficiaries testify that he bequeathed his slave to the witnesses: here the testimony is accepted by agreement because there is no partnership, so no suspicion. Abu Yusuf said: It is not accepted in debt either, because the debt, upon death, becomes attached to the estate; since the dhimmah is destroyed by death. For this reason, if one of them collects his right from the estate, the other shares him in it. Thus the testimony establishes a right of partnership, so suspicion is realized. Unlike during the debtor's life, where testimony of creditors for each other is permissible because it is in the dhimmah due to its continuity, not in the property, so partnership is not realized. Thus in al-Hidayah with a slight addition for clarity. (Fath)
Source pages p. 510

Commentary
This passage from the Book of Wills deals with the ruling on testimony when two groups each claim a bequest from the deceased, and each group testifies in favor of the other. The matn states 'accepted, even if the testimony of each group is for a bequest of a thousand, not for the other,' and the sharh explains that it is accepted because debt is in the dhimmah, which is capable of bearing multiple rights; thus there is no partnership unless the debt arises from a single cause. If a stranger pays the debt of one, the other has no claim to share. This is the view of Muhammad al-Shaybani, with Abu Yusuf opposing. There are varying narrations of Abu Hanifa's position: one with Muhammad, another with Abu Yusuf, and a third from Hasan ibn Ziyad that if they come together and testify, it is void. The commentator then explains that rejection in certain cases is due to the establishment of partnership and consequent tuhma (suspicion of self-interest). For example, if the first pair testifies that the deceased bequeathed his slave to the second pair, and the second pair testifies that he bequeathed one-third to the first pair, it is void. But if the subject of bequest is different (female slave vs. slave), it is accepted unanimously because no partnership is created. Abu Yusuf extends the rejection to debt cases because after death, the debt attaches to the estate, so the dhimmah is no longer existent; thus the testimony creates a partnership in the estate. During the debtor's life, creditors may testify for each other because the debt remains in the dhimmah, not attached to specific property.

Key Terms
شهادة (shahāda): Testimony given in court to prove a claim, specifically in the context of bequests.
وصية (waṣiyya): A bequest made by a person for after their death, up to one-third of the estate without the consent of heirs.
ذمة (dhimma): The legal personality or capacity that bears obligations and rights; during life it is capable of multiple debts, but after death it ceases and debts attach to the estate.
تهمة (tuhma): Suspicion that the witness is testifying out of self-interest or partiality, which renders testimony invalid.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to Muhammad al-Shaybani, why is mutual testimony in bequests accepted?
A) Because the witnesses are not related to the deceased.
B) Because the debts are in the dhimmah, which can hold multiple rights, so no partnership arises.
C) Because the bequests are for less than one-third of the estate.
D) Because the testimony is supported by an oath.

Key Takeaway
Mutual testimony in bequests is accepted when the debts are separate and in the dhimmah, but rejected if it creates a partnership in a single asset.

The Intra-Hanafi Dispute: Abu Yusuf's Objection and the Role of Dhimmah
Intra-Hanafi dispute on the acceptance of mutual testimony in bequests.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain Abu Yusuf's objection to Muhammad's ruling, analyze the role of dhimmah in the dispute, and identify the practical consequence (thamarah al-khilaf).

Core Idea
The fate of the dhimmah after death determines whether mutual testimony creates partnership — Abu Yusuf says it does, Muhammad says it doesn't.

This lesson delves into the intra-Hanafi dispute recorded in the passage. While Muhammad al-Shaybani accepts mutual testimony, Abu Yusuf rejects it in debt cases because he considers the dhimmah destroyed upon death, causing the debt to attach to the estate and create a partnership. We will explore the reasoning of each side and the practical impact.

Guided Path
1
Identify the issue in dispute
The issue is whether mutual testimony in bequests of debt is accepted or rejected. Muhammad says accepted; Abu Yusuf says rejected.
2
Understand Muhammad's reasoning
Muhammad argues that the debt is in the dhimmah, which can hold multiple rights, so no partnership arises. The analogy of a stranger paying one debt without the other having a share supports this.
3
Understand Abu Yusuf's reasoning
Abu Yusuf argues that upon death, the dhimmah is destroyed and the debt attaches to the estate. Thus, if one beneficiary collects from the estate, the other shares, creating partnership and tuhma.
4
Note the varying narrations from Abu Hanifa
Some narrations place Abu Hanifa with Muhammad, some with Abu Yusuf, and al-Hasan reports a third view: if they come together and testify, it is void. This shows the fluidity of the school.
5
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf
Under Muhammad, the testimony is accepted and both claims succeed; under Abu Yusuf, the testimony is rejected and both claims fail.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
كتاب الوصايا
أحكام الشهادة
تقبل، وإن كانت شهادة كل فريق بوصية ألف، لا. للآخر
تقبل: أي تقبل شهادة الفريقين؛ لأن الدين يجب في الذمة، وهي قابلة لحقوق شتى، فلا شركة فيه إذا لم يجب بسبب واحد، ولهذا لو تبرع أجنبي بقضاء دين أحدهما، لم يكن للآخر حق المشاركة، وهذا عند محمد، خلافا لأبي يوسف، ويروى أن أبا حنيفة مع محمد ويروى مع أبي يوسف، وعن أبي يوسف مثل قول محمد، وعن الحسن عن أبي حنيفة أنهم إذا جاءوا معا، وشهدوا فالشهادة باطلة. (فتح عيني) لا: أي لا تقبل الشهادة؛ لأن فيه إثبات الشركة وفيه التهمة، وكذلك إذا شهد الأولان أن الميت أوصى لهذين الرجلين بعبده، وشهد المشهود لهما أنه أوصى للأولين بثلث ماله فهي باطلة؛ لأن الشهادة في هذه الصور مثبتة للشركة، كما في "الهداية"، بخلاف ما إذا شهدا أنه أوصى لهذين الرجلين بجاريته، وشهد المشهود لهما أنه أوصى للشاهدين بعبده، حيث تجوز الشهادة بالاتفاق؛ لعدم الشركة فلا تهمة وقال أبو يوسف: لا تقبل في الدين أيضا؛ لأن الدين بالموت يتعلق بالتركة؛ إذ الذمة خربت بالموت ولهذا لو استوفى أحدهما حقه من التركة يشاركه الآخر فيه، فكانت الشهادة مثبتة حق الشركة فتحققت التهمة بخلاف حال حياة المديون حيث تجوز شهادة الغرماء بعضهم لبعض؛ لأنه في الذمة؛ لبقائها لا في المال، فلا يتحقق الشركة، كذا في "الهداية" بقليل زيادة للإيضاح. (فتح)
Book of Wills. Rulings of Testimony. [It is] accepted, even if the testimony of each group is for a bequest of a thousand, not for the other. [It is] accepted: meaning the testimony of both groups is accepted because the debt is obligated in the dhimmah (legal personality), and it is receptive to various rights, so there is no partnership in it when it is not obligated due to one cause. For this reason, if a stranger voluntarily pays the debt of one of them, the other has no right of participation. This is according to Muhammad, contrary to Abu Yusuf. It is narrated that Abu Hanifa is with Muhammad, and it is narrated that he is with Abu Yusuf. And from Abu Yusuf a statement like Muhammad's. And from al-Hasan from Abu Hanifa: if they come together and testify, the testimony is void. (Fath 'Ayni) 'No': meaning the testimony is not accepted because it involves establishing partnership and there is suspicion (tuhma). Similarly, if the first two testify that the deceased bequeathed his slave to these two men, and the two beneficiaries testify that he bequeathed one-third of his wealth to the first two, it is void because the testimony in these cases establishes partnership, as in al-Hidayah. Contrary to the case where they testify that he bequeathed his female slave to these two men, and the beneficiaries testify that he bequeathed his slave to the witnesses: here the testimony is accepted by agreement because there is no partnership, so no suspicion. Abu Yusuf said: It is not accepted in debt either, because the debt, upon death, becomes attached to the estate; since the dhimmah is destroyed by death. For this reason, if one of them collects his right from the estate, the other shares him in it. Thus the testimony establishes a right of partnership, so suspicion is realized. Unlike during the debtor's life, where testimony of creditors for each other is permissible because it is in the dhimmah due to its continuity, not in the property, so partnership is not realized. Thus in al-Hidayah with a slight addition for clarity. (Fath)
Source pages p. 510

Commentary
This passage from the Book of Wills deals with the ruling on testimony when two groups each claim a bequest from the deceased, and each group testifies in favor of the other. The matn states 'accepted, even if the testimony of each group is for a bequest of a thousand, not for the other,' and the sharh explains that it is accepted because debt is in the dhimmah, which is capable of bearing multiple rights; thus there is no partnership unless the debt arises from a single cause. If a stranger pays the debt of one, the other has no claim to share. This is the view of Muhammad al-Shaybani, with Abu Yusuf opposing. There are varying narrations of Abu Hanifa's position: one with Muhammad, another with Abu Yusuf, and a third from Hasan ibn Ziyad that if they come together and testify, it is void. The commentator then explains that rejection in certain cases is due to the establishment of partnership and consequent tuhma (suspicion of self-interest). For example, if the first pair testifies that the deceased bequeathed his slave to the second pair, and the second pair testifies that he bequeathed one-third to the first pair, it is void. But if the subject of bequest is different (female slave vs. slave), it is accepted unanimously because no partnership is created. Abu Yusuf extends the rejection to debt cases because after death, the debt attaches to the estate, so the dhimmah is no longer existent; thus the testimony creates a partnership in the estate. During the debtor's life, creditors may testify for each other because the debt remains in the dhimmah, not attached to specific property.

Key Terms
شهادة (shahāda): Testimony given in court to prove a claim, specifically in the context of bequests.
وصية (waṣiyya): A bequest made by a person for after their death, up to one-third of the estate without the consent of heirs.
ذمة (dhimma): The legal personality or capacity that bears obligations and rights; during life it is capable of multiple debts, but after death it ceases and debts attach to the estate.
تهمة (tuhma): Suspicion that the witness is testifying out of self-interest or partiality, which renders testimony invalid.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the basis of Abu Yusuf's objection to Muhammad's ruling on mutual testimony in bequests?
A) The dhimmah is destroyed at death, so the debt attaches to the estate, creating partnership.
B) The witnesses are not reliable because they are not heirs.
C) The bequests are for more than one-third of the estate.
D) The testimony is not corroborated by an oath.

Key Takeaway
The intra-Hanafi dispute on mutual testimony in bequests hinges on whether the dhimmah remains intact after death; this determines if partnership and tuhma arise.
